   Explanation: Engineers have a duty to ensure designs are accurate and reliable. Reporting and correcting errors, even if they cause delays, upholds professional standards and fosters trust in engineering practices.

45. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Engineers should not sign documents or approve work they do not fully understand. Requesting clarification ensures that you uphold ethical and professional responsibilities while maintaining the integrity of the project.

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Engineering Economics

1. A company plans to invest $10,000 in a project that will generate $1,500 annually for 10 years. If the interest rate is 8%, what is the net present value (NPV) of the project?
   A) $1,490
   B) $2,330
   C) $3,780
   D) $4,860

2. Which cost type is most likely categorized as a fixed cost in manufacturing?
   A) Raw materials
   B) Production labor
   C) Building rent
   D) Utilities

3. A machine costing $40,000 has an estimated life of 10 years and a salvage value of $5,000. Using the straight-line depreciation method, what is the annual depreciation expense?
   A) $3,500
   B) $4,000
   C) $5,000
   D) $5,500

4. A factory produces widgets with a variable cost of $25 per unit and fixed costs of $50,000 annually. If the selling price per widget is $40, how many units must be sold to break even?
   A) 2,000 units
   B) 3,333 units
   C) 4,000 units
   D) 5,000 units

5. What is the future value of an investment of $5,000 made today at an annual interest rate of 10%, compounded yearly, after 5 years?
   A) $7,500
   B) $8,052
   C) $8,805
   D) $9,050

6. Which of the following represents an effective annual rate (EAR) if the nominal interest rate is 12% compounded monthly?
   A) 12.00%
   B) 12.68%
   C) 13.00%
   D) 12.10%

7. A project requires an initial investment of $20,000 and generates $5,000 annually. What is the payback period?
   A) 3 years
   B) 4 years
   C) 5 years
   D) 6 years

8. If the inflation rate is 4% per year, what is the real interest rate when the nominal interest rate is 7%?
   A) 2.88%
   B) 3.00%
   C) 3.85%
   D) 4.00%

9. A project has a 60% chance of earning $15,000 and a 40% chance of losing $5,000. What is the expected monetary value (EMV) of the project?
   A) $6,000
   B) $7,000
   C) $8,000
   D) $9,000

10. Which of the following is NOT a commonly used criterion for evaluating the economic feasibility of a project?
   A) NPV
   B) Payback Period
   C) Risk-Free Rate
   D) IRR

11. A project has IRR of 10% and the discount rate is 8%. What should be the decision?
   A) Accept the project
   B) Reject the project
   C) Neutral decision
   D) Request further analysis

12. If choosing Project A means forgoing Project B, which would have earned $8,000, what is the opportunity cost of selecting Project A?
   A) $4,000
   B) $8,000
   C) $10,000
   D) $12,000

13. A piece of equipment has a book value of $15,000 after 5 years. If it is sold for $12,000, what is the capital loss?
   A) $2,000
   B) $3,000
   C) $3,500
   D) $4,000

14. If a company’s taxable income is $50,000 and its tax rate is 30%, what is the tax liability?
   A) $12,000
   B) $15,000
   C) $18,000
   D) $20,000

15. Which estimation technique uses historical data to predict future costs?
   A) Top-down estimation
   B) Bottom-up estimation
   C) Analogous estimation
   D) Parametric estimation

16. Sensitivity analysis primarily evaluates which aspect of a project?
   A) Project scope
   B) Variable uncertainty
   C) Market trends
   D) Project timeline

17. Which capital budgeting method considers both the time value of money and cash flows?
   A) Payback Period
   B) Accounting Rate of Return
   C) Net Present Value
   D) Future Value Method

18. A project’s profitability index is 1.2. What does this indicate?
   A) The project is not profitable.
   B) The project is marginally acceptable.
   C) The project will generate returns above costs.
   D) The project requires further evaluation.

19. If electricity costs increase at a rate of 6% annually, what will a $1,000 electricity bill cost after 3 years?
   A) $1,179
   B) $1,191
   C) $1,201
   D) $1,250

20. What is the economic life of an asset defined as?
   A) The time until the asset physically breaks down.
   B) The time during which the asset is economically worthwhile to own.
   C) The total time expected for asset usage.
   D) The time at which the asset reaches salvage value.

21. A company considers two projects: Project X requires an initial investment of $50,000 and generates $12,000 annually for 6 years. Project Y requires $40,000 and generates $10,000 annually for 4 years. If the discount rate is 10%, which project has the higher present worth?
   A) Project X
   B) Project Y
   C) Both projects have the same present worth
   D) Cannot be determined from the given data

22. A company is evaluating two mutually exclusive projects, A and B. Project A has an IRR of 15%, while Project B's IRR is 12%. The company's cost of capital is 10%. Which project should the company choose?
   A) Project A
   B) Project B
   C) Both projects should be chosen
   D) Neither project should be chosen

23. A machine costing $100,000 is expected to have a salvage value of $10,000 after 8 years. Using the double-declining balance method, what is the depreciation expense for the first year?
   A) $25,000
   B) $20,000
   C) $22,500
   D) $15,000

24. A factory produces 10,000 units annually with a fixed cost of $60,000 and a variable cost of $8 per unit. If the selling price per unit is $12, what is the breakeven volume?
   A) 15,000 units
   B) 10,000 units
   C) 5,000 units
   D) 20,000 units

25. An investor deposits $5,000 in an account that earns 6% annual interest compounded quarterly. What will the value of the account be after 5 years?
   A) $6,734.50
   B) $6,744.25
   C) $6,750.55
   D) $6,780.20

26. If a construction project has a budget of $500,000 and the inflation rate is expected to be 3% annually, what will be the adjusted budget in 5 years?
   A) $579,000
   B) $580,000
   C) $580,800
   D) $585,900

27. A project has a net cash inflow of $10,000 annually and requires an initial investment of $60,000. Using a discount rate of 8%, what is the net present value (NPV) of the project?
   A) $4,580
   B) $6,580
   C) $8,580
   D) $10,580

28. A company is deciding between two investment options: Option A has a 70% chance of yielding $20,000 and a 30% chance of losing $5,000. Option B has a 50% chance of yielding $25,000 and a 50% chance of breaking even. Which option is economically better based on expected value?
   A) Option A
   B) Option B
   C) Both options are equally good
   D) Cannot be determined

29. A factory can produce 100 additional units at a variable cost of $25 per unit. If the selling price per unit is $40, how much profit will be generated from the additional production?
   A) $1,000
   B) $1,500
   C) $2,000
   D) $3,000

30. A project requires an initial investment of $100,000 and generates $25,000 annually. What is the payback period for this project?
   A) 3 years
   B) 4 years
   C) 5 years
   D) 6 years

31. A company is deciding between two projects: Project A has an expected net cash flow of $25,000 annually for 8 years with an initial investment of $120,000, while Project B has an expected net cash flow of $40,000 annually for 5 years with an initial investment of $160,000. Assuming a discount rate of 10%, which project has the higher Net Present Value (NPV)?
   A) Project A
   B) Project B
   C) Both projects have the same NPV
   D) Not enough information provided

32. A manufacturing facility is considering purchasing a machine that costs $80,000 and has annual maintenance costs of $5,000. It will generate annual savings of $20,000 in operations and has a lifespan of 10 years. If the discount rate is 8%, what is the machine’s equivalent annual cost (EAC)?
   A) $10,000
   B) $15,000
   C) $18,000
   D) $20,000

33. A company is planning to replace a machine with a new model costing $150,000. The old machine has a salvage value of $30,000 and annual running costs of $25,000. The new model has annual running costs of $10,000 and a lifespan of 12 years. What is the return on investment (ROI) for purchasing the new model?
   A) 16.7%
   B) 20%
   C) 25%
   D) 30%

34. Which of the following describes the concept of sunk cost in engineering economics?
   A) The initial investment for a project
   B) Costs that cannot be recovered and should not influence future decisions
   C) Costs related to variable expenses
   D) Costs associated with future cash flows

35. A company estimates a project will generate $10,000 annually for 5 years. The initial investment is $35,000, and the discount rate is 12%. What is the Present Worth (PW) of the project?
   A) $38,000
   B) $28,000
   C) $44,000
   D) $50,000

36. A company borrows $50,000 at an annual interest rate of 6%, compounded monthly. What will be the total amount owed after 7 years?
   A) $71,000
   B) $76,000
   C) $79,000
   D) $82,000

37. What is the breakeven point (in units) for a factory with fixed costs of $80,000, a variable cost per unit of $15, and a selling price of $25 per unit?
   A) 4,000 units
   B) 5,000 units
   C) 6,000 units
   D) 8,000 units

38. If a project has a Benefit-to-Cost ratio (B/C) of 1.2, which decision should be made?
   A) Reject the project
   B) Accept the project
   C) Reevaluate with a lower discount rate
   D) Accept only if it has no opportunity cost

39. A piece of equipment has a market value of $25,000, a salvage value of $5,000, and accumulated depreciation of $15,000. What is its book value?
   A) $5,000
   B) $10,000
   C) $15,000
   D) $25,000

40. What is the primary purpose of conducting a sensitivity analysis in economic feasibility studies?
   A) To compare multiple projects
   B) To evaluate how changes in key variables affect project outcomes
   C) To determine the net present value (NPV)
   D) To calculate depreciation rates

41. A project generates cash flows of $12,000 in Year 1, $15,000 in Year 2, and $20,000 in Year 3. If the discount rate is 10%, what is the total present value of these cash flows?
   A) $41,000
   B) $42,000
   C) $44,000
   D) $45,000

42. A company plans to save $10,000 annually in an account earning 5% interest compounded yearly. How much will the company have saved after 10 years?
   A) $105,000
   B) $120,000
   C) $126,000
   D) $132,000

43. Which method accounts for the time value of money when comparing projects?
   A) Payback period
   B) Net Present Value
   C) Variable cost analysis
   D) Breakeven analysis

44. If a company invests $50,000 in a project with a life span of 5 years, and the project generates $15,000 annually at a discount rate of 12%, what is the project's profitability index?
   A) 1.15
   B) 1.30
   C) 1.45
   D) 1.60

45. A machine costing $80,000 has a salvage value of $8,000 and a life span of 10 years. Using straight-line depreciation, what is the annual depreciation expense?
   A) $7,000
   B) $7,200
   C) $7,500
   D) $8,000

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: To calculate the NPV, use the formula NPV = Σ(Cash Flow/(1 + r)^t) - Initial Investment. Summing cash flows over 10 years discounted at 8% and subtracting $10,000 results in $2,330.

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Building rent is classified as a fixed cost because it does not change with the level of production.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Straight-line depreciation is calculated as (Cost - Salvage Value) / Useful Life, which equals ($40,000 - $5,000) / 10 = $3,500.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Break-even point = Fixed Costs / (Selling Price - Variable Cost). $50,000 / ($40 - $25) = 3,333 units.

5. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Future Value = P(1 + r)^t = $5,000(1 + 0.10)^5 = $8,805.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: EAR = (1 + r/n)^(n*t) - 1. For monthly compounding: EAR = (1 + 0.12/12)^(12*1) - 1 = 12.68%.

7. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Payback Period = Initial Investment / Annual Cash Flow = $20,000 / $5,000 = 4 years.

8. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Real Interest Rate = (1 + Nominal Rate) / (1 + Inflation Rate) - 1 = (1 + 0.07) / (1 + 0.04) - 1 = 2.88%.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: EMV = (Probability1 * Outcome1) + (Probability2 * Outcome2). EMV = (0.6 * $15,000) + (0.4 * -$5,000) = $9,000.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The Risk-Free Rate describes a theoretical return on investment and is not typically used directly in feasibility evaluations like NPV, Payback Period, or IRR.

11. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Accept the project if IRR > discount rate, as it indicates the project will generate returns above the required rate.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Opportunity cost is the value of the next best alternative forgone, which in this case is $8,000 from Project B.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Capital loss = Book Value - Sale Price = $15,000 - $12,000 = $3,000.

14. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Tax Liability = Taxable Income * Tax Rate = $50,000 * 0.30 = $15,000.

15. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Analogous estimation uses historical data from similar projects to estimate costs.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Sensitivity analysis assesses how changes in key variables affect the outcome of a project.

17. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: NPV incorporates both the time value of money and projected cash inflows/outflows.

18. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Profitability Index > 1 signifies that the project will yield returns exceeding its costs.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Future Cost = Present Cost * (1 + Rate)^Years = $1,000 * (1 + 0.06)^3 = $1,179.

20. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Economic life describes the duration over which an asset remains cost-effective to utilize.

21. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Calculate the present worth for both projects using the formula PW = CF × [(1 - (1 + r)^-n) / r] and compare the results.

22. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Project A has a higher IRR than Project B and both exceed the company's cost of capital, making Project A the better option.

23. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Double-declining balance method uses the formula Depreciation = 2 × (Book Value / Useful Life). First-year depreciation is calculated as 2 × (100,000 / 8).

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Breakeven volume is calculated as Fixed Costs / (Selling Price - Variable Cost). Here, breakeven volume = 60,000 / (12 - 8).

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use the formula FV = P × (1 + r/n)^(n×t), substituting r = 0.06, n = 4, and t = 5.

26. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Use the formula Future Value = Present Value × (1 + Inflation Rate)^Years.

27. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Calculate NPV using the formula NPV = ∑(CF / (1 + r)^t) - Initial Investment.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Calculate expected value for both options and compare. Expected Value = Probability × Outcome.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Profit = (Selling Price - Variable Cost) × Quantity. Here, profit = (40 - 25) × 100.

30. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Payback Period = Initial Investment / Annual Cash Flow. Here, Payback Period = 100,000 / 25,000.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: To calculate NPV, discount cash flows to the present value using the formula PV = CF / (1 + r)^n. Project A provides a higher NPV due to its longer cash flow duration despite the lower annual cash flow.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: To find EAC, sum the annualized capital cost (calculated using the discount rate and lifespan) and the annual maintenance cost. The machine’s EAC is approximately $15,000.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: ROI is calculated as (Savings - Investment Cost) / Investment Cost. Annual savings are $15,000, and the total savings over 12 years exceeds the investment cost, resulting in a 20% ROI.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Sunk costs are past expenditures that cannot be recovered and should not be considered when analyzing future economic decisions.

35. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Present Worth (PW) is calculated by discounting future cash flows back to their present value using a given discount rate. The PW of the project accounts for both the cash inflows and the initial investment.

36. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total amount owed is calculated using the compound interest formula A = P(1 + r/n)^(nt). Monthly compounding significantly affects the future value.

37. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The breakeven point is calculated using the formula Fixed Costs / (Selling Price - Variable Cost). For this scenario, breakeven occurs at 5,000 units.

38. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A Benefit-to-Cost ratio greater than 1 signifies the project generates more benefits than costs and should be accepted.

39. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The book value of a piece of equipment is the original cost minus accumulated depreciation.

40. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Sensitivity analysis is used to assess how changes in input variables, such as costs or revenue, affect the outcomes of a project.

41. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Present Value of cash flows is calculated for each year using PV = CF / (1 + r)^n and summed to find the total.

42. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The future value of annuities can be calculated using FV = Pmt × [(1 + r)^n − 1] / r, where r is the interest rate and n is the number of periods.

43. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Net Present Value (NPV) evaluates projects by discounting future cash flows to their present value, incorporating the time value of money.

44. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Profitability Index (PI) is calculated as the Present Value of future cash flows divided by the initial investment. Here, PI = PV / Initial Investment.

45. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Straight-line depreciation is calculated as (Cost − Salvage Value) / Life Span. Here, the annual depreciation expense is $7,000.

1. Two point charges, q1 = +3 μC and q2 = -5 μC, are placed 0.2 m apart in a vacuum. What is the magnitude of the electrostatic force between the charges? (Use k = 8.99 x 10^9 N·m²/C²)
   A) 3.37 N
   B) 4.49 N
   C) 5.62 N
   D) 6.74 N

   A) 7.54 x 10^-3 T
   B) 1.51 x 10^-3 T
   C) 4.77 x 10^-3 T
   D) 2.52 x 10^-3 T

   B) 15.6 Ω
   C) 19.8 Ω
   D) 22.5 Ω

   A) 0.25 T
   B) 0.50 T
   C) 0.75 T
   D) 1.00 T

   D) 4.18 V

   D) 500 N

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: To solve, use the equations of equilibrium. Summing moments about the farther support gives the reaction force at the closer support as R = (200 N × 3 m + 100 N × 2.5 m) / 5 m = 250 N.

2. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the equilibrium equations and the friction limit at the base, the maximum height is determined by balancing torques about the base while considering friction. The calculations give a maximum height of 4.5 m.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: By resolving forces vertically and horizontally and considering the geometry of the structure, member BC is found to carry a force of 353.55 N in tension.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The centroid of a semicircular plate is located at 4R/3π from the flat edge along the axis of symmetry.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The limiting friction force is μN = 0.5 × 400 × cos(30°). The weight component down the plane is 400 × sin(30°). Since the friction force exceeds the weight component, the box will not slide.

6. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: By resolving forces horizontally and vertically, and applying equilibrium, the tension in the cable on the 60° side is found to be 1155 N.

7. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The moment of inertia about the base is calculated using I = (1/3) bh³ = (1/3)(2)(3³) = 18 m⁴.

8. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Since the load is symmetrical, the reactions at both supports are equal, and each is 150 N.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The vertical members counteract the load, resulting in compressive forces to maintain equilibrium.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The resultant force is the vector sum of the horizontal and vertical forces: R = √(500² + 300²) = 583 N.

11. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the equations of equilibrium: sum of vertical forces equals zero and sum of moments equals zero, the reaction at the right support is calculated as 300 N.

12. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: By resolving forces in horizontal and vertical directions and using trigonometric relationships, the tension in the 30° rope is found to be 2887 N.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The centroid is calculated using the weighted average of the centroids of the rectangle and semicircle. The result is 3.33 m.

14. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the method of joints, the diagonal member closest to the center is found to be in 10 kN tension due to the symmetry of the load.

15. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The static friction force is calculated as μN = 0.4 × (50 × 9.81) = 250 N. This is the minimum force required.

16. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum bending moment for a uniformly loaded simply supported beam occurs at the center and is calculated as wL²/8 = (5 × 8²)/8 = 40 kN·m.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Since the wall is smooth, there is no vertical reaction there. The normal reaction at the base equals the total vertical load, which is 600 N.

18. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: By resolving forces horizontally, the horizontal components cancel each other, resulting in a reaction of 0 kN.

19. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The moment of inertia about the base is given by (1/3)bh³ = (1/3) × 3 × 6³ = 108 m⁴.

20. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The maximum static friction force (μN) is greater than the component of the weight parallel to the plane. Hence, the block does not slide.

21. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total weight of the sign and the bar is 1000 N. Since the sign is at the center of the bar and the bar is symmetric, the load is equally distributed between the two cables. Each cable bears half the load: 1000 N ÷ 2 = 500 N.

22. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In a Warren truss, loads are transmitted through diagonal and horizontal members. The diagonal member closest to the load experiences the maximum force because it directly transfers the applied horizontal load.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The maximum static friction force is calculated as f = μ × N = 0.5 × 150 N = 75 N. Since the applied force of 60 N is less than the maximum static friction force, the block will not move.

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The centroid of a triangle is located at a distance of 2/3 the height from the base and 1/3 the base length from the vertex.

25. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The moment about the supported end is calculated as M = Force × Distance = 300 N × 7 m = 2100 Nm.

26. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The total load can be calculated using the area of the triangle: (1/2) × base × height = (1/2) × 6 m × 400 N/m = 1200 N.

27. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Using vector addition and resolving forces into components, the resultant magnitude is √(Rx² + Ry²), resulting in approximately 265 N.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Since the beam is symmetric and the load is at its center, the force is equally distributed. Thus, each vertical member supports 250 N.

29. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Cables under tensile loads primarily experience axial tension, which is the internal force resisting elongation.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The tension horizontal component is T × sin(45°). The vertical force equals the object's weight (mg = 200 × 9.8). From equilibrium, T = mg/cos(45°), and solving gives the horizontal component as 980 N.

31. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the equilibrium equations, the sum of moments about the pin support gives the reaction at the roller. Summing vertical forces yields the reaction at the pin.

   Explanation: The force in the diagonal member can be calculated using method of joints and equilibrium equations at the center joint.

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Statics

1. A 5 kg box is sliding down a frictionless incline making a 30° angle with the horizontal. What is the acceleration of the box along the incline?
   A) 4.9 m/s²
   B) 9.8 m/s²
   C) 8.5 m/s²
   D) 3.3 m/s²

2. A car accelerates uniformly from rest to a speed of 20 m/s over a distance of 100 meters. What is the car’s acceleration?
   A) 2 m/s²
   B) 4 m/s²
   C) 1 m/s²
   D) 3 m/s²

3. A mass-spring system with a spring constant of 200 N/m and a mass of 2 kg is undergoing simple harmonic motion. What is its natural frequency?
   A) 10 Hz
   B) 5 Hz
   C) 1.6 Hz
   D) 3.2 Hz

4. A 15 kg object is being pushed horizontally with a force of 60 N. If the coefficient of kinetic friction is 0.2, what is the object’s acceleration?
   A) 2 m/s²
   B) 1.6 m/s²
   C) 3 m/s²
   D) 4 m/s²

5. A projectile is launched at an angle of 45° with an initial velocity of 14 m/s. What is the maximum height it reaches?
   A) 5.0 m
   B) 7.0 m
   C) 10.0 m
   D) 14.0 m

125. A simple pendulum with a length of 1.5 m is released from an angular displacement of 10°. What is the maximum speed of the pendulum bob? Assume small angle approximation and g = 9.8 m/s².
   A) 0.56 m/s
   B) 0.68 m/s
   C) 0.80 m/s
   D) 0.92 m/s

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---
1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The acceleration is calculated as a = g * sin(θ). Substituting g = 9.8 m/s² and θ = 30°, we get a = 9.8 * sin(30°) = 4.9 m/s².

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the kinematic equation v² = u² + 2as, where v = 20 m/s, u = 0 m/s, and s = 100 m, solving for a gives a = v² / (2s) = (20)² / (2 * 100) = 2 m/s².

3. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The natural frequency is given by f = (1/2π) * √(k/m). Substituting k = 200 N/m and m = 2 kg, f = (1/2π) * √(200/2) = 1.6 Hz.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Net force is F_net = F_applied - F_friction. F_friction = μ * N = μ * m * g. Substituting μ = 0.2, m = 15 kg, g = 9.8 m/s², F_friction = 0.2 * 15 * 9.8 = 29.4 N. Net force = 60 - 29.4 = 30.6 N. Acceleration = F_net / m = 30.6 / 15 = 1.6 m/s².

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The maximum height is given by h = (v₀² * sin²θ) / (2g). Substituting v₀ = 14 m/s, θ = 45°, and g = 9.8 m/s², h = (14² * sin²(45)) / (2 * 9.8) = 7.0 m.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The damped frequency ω_d is given by ω_d = ω_n * √(1 - ζ²), where ζ = damping ratio and ω_n = undamped natural frequency. Substituting ζ = 0.5, ω_n = 8 rad/s, ω_d = 8 * √(1 - 0.5²) = 6.9 rad/s.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Centripetal acceleration is a_c = v² / r. Substituting v = 4 m/s and r = 2 m, a_c = (4²) / 2 = 8 m/s².

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the equation s = ut + 0.5at², where u = 0, a = 2 m/s², and t = 10 s, s = 0 + 0.5 * 2 * (10)² = 100 m.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The period of a pendulum is T = 2π√(L/g). Substituting L = 0.5 m and g = 9.8 m/s², T = 2π√(0.5/9.8) ≈ 1.4 s.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Centripetal force is F_c = mv² / r. Substituting m = 1000 kg, v = 20 m/s, and r = 50 m, F_c = (1000 * 20²) / 50 = 16000 N.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The acceleration is calculated by resolving the forces into components, accounting for the effect of friction, and applying Newton's second law.

   Explanation: The distance is calculated using the equation s = ut + 0.5at², where u is the initial velocity and a is the deceleration.

   Explanation: Maximum height is given by h = (v₀²sin²θ)/(2g). Substituting v₀ = 25 m/s, θ = 45°, and g = 9.8 m/s² gives h = (25² × sin²45)/(2 × 9.8) ≈ 31.88 m.

112. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Critical damping coefficient is given by c_critical = 2√(km). Substituting k = 200 N/m and m = 3 kg gives c_critical = 2√(200 × 3) ≈ 49 Ns/m.

113. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Angular acceleration is given by α = (ω₂ - ω₁)/t. Substituting ω₁ = 10 rad/s, ω₂ = 20 rad/s, and t = 5 s gives α = (20 - 10)/5 = 2 rad/s².

114. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the work-energy principle, first calculate the net force acting on the object, considering both the applied force and frictional force. Then, determine the deceleration and solve for the stopping distance.

115. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Solve using the kinematic equation y = v₀t + 0.5gt², where y is the given height, v₀ is the initial velocity, and g is the acceleration due to gravity.

116. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total energy of a spring-mass system is given by E = 0.5kA², where k is the spring constant and A is the amplitude.

117. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Resolve the force into horizontal and vertical components, calculate the frictional force, and use Newton's second law to find the net acceleration.

118. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Integrate the velocity function v(t) = 3t² - 2t over the given time interval to find the displacement.

119. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The period of a mass-spring system is given by T = 2π√(m/k), where m is the mass and k is the spring constant.

120. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Calculate the component of the gravitational force along the incline and the maximum static frictional force. Find the additional force required for equilibrium.

121. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use the kinematic equation v² = u² + 2as to solve for the acceleration, where v is the final velocity, u is the initial velocity, and s is the distance.

122. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The damping ratio is given by ζ = c / (2√(mk)), where c is the damping coefficient, m is the mass, and k is the spring constant.

123. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Work done is the integral of the force over displacement: W = ∫ F(x) dx from x = 2 to x = 5.

124. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For rolling without slipping, the relationship v = rω holds. Solve for angular velocity ω = v/r.

125. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Compute the maximum speed using energy conservation: mgh = 0.5mv², where h = L(1 - cosθ).

1. A 5 kg box is sliding down a frictionless incline making a 30° angle with the horizontal. What is the acceleration of the box along the incline?
   A) 4.9 m/s²
   B) 9.8 m/s²
   C) 8.5 m/s²
   D) 3.3 m/s²

   A) 2 m/s²
   B) 4 m/s²
   C) 1 m/s²
   D) 3 m/s²

   D) 3.2 Hz

   D) 4 m/s²

   D) 7.5 rad/s

125. A simple pendulum with a length of 1.5 m is released from an angular displacement of 10°. What is the maximum speed of the pendulum bob? Assume small angle approximation and g = 9.8 m/s².
   A) 0.56 m/s
   B) 0.68 m/s
   C) 0.80 m/s
   D) 0.92 m/s

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---
1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The acceleration is calculated as a = g * sin(θ). Substituting g = 9.8 m/s² and θ = 30°, we get a = 9.8 * sin(30°) = 4.9 m/s².

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the kinematic equation v² = u² + 2as, where v = 20 m/s, u = 0 m/s, and s = 100 m, solving for a gives a = v² / (2s) = (20)² / (2 * 100) = 2 m/s².

3. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The natural frequency is given by f = (1/2π) * √(k/m). Substituting k = 200 N/m and m = 2 kg, f = (1/2π) * √(200/2) = 1.6 Hz.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Net force is F_net = F_applied - F_friction. F_friction = μ * N = μ * m * g. Substituting μ = 0.2, m = 15 kg, g = 9.8 m/s², F_friction = 0.2 * 15 * 9.8 = 29.4 N. Net force = 60 - 29.4 = 30.6 N. Acceleration = F_net / m = 30.6 / 15 = 1.6 m/s².

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The maximum height is given by h = (v₀² * sin²θ) / (2g). Substituting v₀ = 14 m/s, θ = 45°, and g = 9.8 m/s², h = (14² * sin²(45)) / (2 * 9.8) = 7.0 m.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The damped frequency ω_d is given by ω_d = ω_n * √(1 - ζ²), where ζ = damping ratio and ω_n = undamped natural frequency. Substituting ζ = 0.5, ω_n = 8 rad/s, ω_d = 8 * √(1 - 0.5²) = 6.9 rad/s.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Centripetal acceleration is a_c = v² / r. Substituting v = 4 m/s and r = 2 m, a_c = (4²) / 2 = 8 m/s².

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the equation s = ut + 0.5at², where u = 0, a = 2 m/s², and t = 10 s, s = 0 + 0.5 * 2 * (10)² = 100 m.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The period of a pendulum is T = 2π√(L/g). Substituting L = 0.5 m and g = 9.8 m/s², T = 2π√(0.5/9.8) ≈ 1.4 s.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Centripetal force is F_c = mv² / r. Substituting m = 1000 kg, v = 20 m/s, and r = 50 m, F_c = (1000 * 20²) / 50 = 16000 N.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The acceleration is calculated by resolving the forces into components, accounting for the effect of friction, and applying Newton's second law.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: At maximum height, the velocity becomes zero. Using the equation v = u + at, where u is the initial velocity and a is the acceleration due to gravity (-9.8 m/s²), solve for t.

13. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The natural frequency is calculated using ω = √(k/m), where k is the spring constant and m is the mass.

14. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Centripetal force is calculated using Fc = mv²/r, where m is the mass, v is the speed, and r is the radius of the circular path.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The distance is calculated using the equation s = ut + 0.5at², where u is the initial velocity and a is the deceleration.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The damping ratio is calculated using ζ = c / (2√(km)), where c is the damping coefficient, k is the spring constant, and m is the mass.

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The acceleration is found by resolving forces parallel to the incline, factoring in the frictional force, and using Newton's second law.

18. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The final velocity is calculated using v = u + at, where u is the initial velocity (0 m/s) and a is the acceleration.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The period of a pendulum is calculated using T = 2π√(L/g), where L is the length and g is the gravitational acceleration.

20. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The orbital speed is calculated using v = √(GM/r), where G is the gravitational constant, M is Earth's mass, and r is the orbital radius.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Since the crate is moving at a constant velocity, the net force along the incline is zero. The applied force must counteract both the parallel component of weight and the friction force. F_applied = m*g*sin(20°) + μ_k*m*g*cos(20°).

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The acceleration is (v_f - v_i)/t = 4 m/s². Using the kinematic equation s = v_i*t + 0.5*a*t², we find s = 10*5 + 0.5*4*5² = 125 m.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The damped natural frequency is calculated as ω_d = ω_n*sqrt(1 - ζ²). Substituting, ω_d = 10*sqrt(1 - 0.8²) = 8 rad/s.

24. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The horizontal component of the force is F_x = F*cos(θ). The horizontal acceleration is a_x = F_x/m = (10*cos(60°))/2 = 4.33 m/s².

25. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The time of flight is determined by vertical motion: t = sqrt(2h/g). The horizontal distance is x = v_x*t = 10*sqrt(2*50/9.8) ≈ 30 m.

26. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The angular frequency is given by ω = sqrt(k/m). Substituting, ω = sqrt(250/5) = 7 rad/s.

The net force causing acceleration is F_net = 80 - (0.3 * 20 * 9.81) = 21.87 N, so the box will accelerate.

45. Correct Answer: B

From v² = u² + 2a*s, we calculate the additional height h2 = (50²)/(2*9.81) = 115 m. The total height is h1 + h2 = 140 + 115 = 255 m.

92. Correct Answer: A

93. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Angular frequency ω is calculated as ω = sqrt(k/m) = sqrt(300/4) ≈ 8.66 rad/s.

94. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Net force is calculated by resolving the applied force and accounting for friction. F_net = F_horizontal - F_friction. Then, a = F_net/m.

95. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using v² = u² + 2as, we solve for a. Here, 12² = 0 + 2*a*24, a = 3.0 m/s².

96. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Damping ratio ζ = c / (2*sqrt(k*m)). Substituting ζ = 20 / (2*sqrt(100*5)) = 0.4.

97. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using impulse-momentum theorem, v = (1/m)∫F(t) dt from 0 to 4. v = (1/2) * ∫5t dt = 30 m/s.

98. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using v² = u² + 2as, s = u²/(2*a) = 25²/(2*5) = 125 m.

99. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum velocity v_max = ω*A = 5*0.1 = 1.0 m/s.

100. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using v² = u² + 2as. First calculate a = F/m = 5000/1000. Then v² = 0 + 2(5)(50) = 500, v = 20 m/s.

101. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Time to fall is t = sqrt(2h/g) = sqrt(2*80/9.8) ≈ 3.2 s.

102. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Period is T = 1/f = 1/2 = 0.5 s.

103. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Resolve the force components and calculate net force considering friction. Use a = F_net/m.

104. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The net force is 18 N - 10 N = 8 N. Acceleration is given by F = ma, so a = F/m = 8/6 = 1.33 m/s².

105. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the equation v² = u² + 2as, where v = 0, u = 15 m/s, and a = -3 m/s²: 0 = (15)² + 2(-3)s. Solving for s gives s = 37.5 m.

106. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The natural frequency is given by f = (1/2π)√(k/m). Substituting k = 150 and m = 5 gives f = 3.09 Hz.

107. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The frictional force is F_f = µN = 0.4 × (10 × 9.8) = 39.2 N. Net force = applied force - frictional force = 80 - 39.2 = 40.8 N. Acceleration = net force / mass = 40.8 / 10 = 1.6 m/s².

108. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Use the equation s = (1/2)gt². Solving for t: t² = 2s/g = 2(60)/9.8; t = √(12.24) ≈ 2.81 s.

109. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The damped angular frequency is ω_d = √(ω₀² - (c/(2m))²), where ω₀ = √(k/m). ω₀ = √(100/2) = 7.07 rad/s, c/(2m) = 20/(2×2) = 5. Solving gives ω_d = √(7.07² - 5²) ≈ 6.32 rad/s.

110. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Centripetal force is given by F_c = mv²/r. Substituting m = 12 kg, v = 6 m/s, and r = 3 m gives F_c = (12 × 6²) / 3 = 192 N.

111. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum height is given by h = (v₀²sin²θ)/(2g). Substituting v₀ = 25 m/s, θ = 45°, and g = 9.8 m/s² gives h = (25² × sin²45)/(2 × 9.8) ≈ 31.88 m.

112. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Critical damping coefficient is given by c_critical = 2√(km). Substituting k = 200 N/m and m = 3 kg gives c_critical = 2√(200 × 3) ≈ 49 Ns/m.

113. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Angular acceleration is given by α = (ω₂ - ω₁)/t. Substituting ω₁ = 10 rad/s, ω₂ = 20 rad/s, and t = 5 s gives α = (20 - 10)/5 = 2 rad/s².

114. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using the work-energy principle, first calculate the net force acting on the object, considering both the applied force and frictional force. Then, determine the deceleration and solve for the stopping distance.

115. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Solve using the kinematic equation y = v₀t + 0.5gt², where y is the given height, v₀ is the initial velocity, and g is the acceleration due to gravity.

116. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The total energy of a spring-mass system is given by E = 0.5kA², where k is the spring constant and A is the amplitude.

117. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Resolve the force into horizontal and vertical components, calculate the frictional force, and use Newton's second law to find the net acceleration.

118. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Integrate the velocity function v(t) = 3t² - 2t over the given time interval to find the displacement.

119. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The period of a mass-spring system is given by T = 2π√(m/k), where m is the mass and k is the spring constant.

120. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Calculate the component of the gravitational force along the incline and the maximum static frictional force. Find the additional force required for equilibrium.

121. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use the kinematic equation v² = u² + 2as to solve for the acceleration, where v is the final velocity, u is the initial velocity, and s is the distance.

122. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The damping ratio is given by ζ = c / (2√(mk)), where c is the damping coefficient, m is the mass, and k is the spring constant.

123. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Work done is the integral of the force over displacement: W = ∫ F(x) dx from x = 2 to x = 5.

124. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For rolling without slipping, the relationship v = rω holds. Solve for angular velocity ω = v/r.

125. Correct Answer: B

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Mechanics of Materials

1. A steel rod with a diameter of 20 mm is subjected to an axial tensile force of 40 kN. Assuming the modulus of elasticity is 200 GPa, what is the elongation of the rod if its length is 2 meters?
   A) 0.4 mm
   B) 0.2 mm
   C) 0.8 mm
   D) 1.0 mm

2. A bar of uniform cross-section is subjected to a tensile load of 50 kN. The bar measures 1.5 meters in length and has an elastic modulus of 210 GPa. The stress induced is 100 MPa. What is the strain in the bar?
   A) 0.000476
   B) 0.0005
   C) 0.0006
   D) 0.0007

3. A solid circular shaft is required to transmit 200 Nm of torque. If the maximum shear stress is limited to 50 MPa and the shaft’s diameter is to be determined, what is the required diameter?
   A) 28.3 mm
   B) 31.2 mm
   C) 35.4 mm
   D) 40.0 mm

4. A simply supported beam with a length of 6 meters is subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 2 kN/m. What is the maximum bending moment in the beam?
   A) 9 kNm
   B) 12 kNm
   C) 18 kNm
   D) 24 kNm

5. A machine component is subjected to a tensile stress of 120 MPa and a shear stress of 40 MPa. What is the maximum principal stress in the component?
   A) 130 MPa
   B) 140 MPa
   C) 160 MPa
   D) 180 MPa

6. A material is subjected to a normal stress of 50 MPa and shear stress of 30 MPa. Calculate the radius of the Mohr’s circle.
   A) 20 MPa
   B) 30 MPa
   C) 40 MPa
   D) 50 MPa

7. A cantilever beam with a length of 4 meters is subjected to a point load of 500 N at its free end. The flexural rigidity (EI) of the beam is 1 × 10⁶ N·m². Calculate the deflection at the free end.
   A) 8 mm
   B) 10 mm
   C) 12 mm
   D) 16 mm

8. A slender column with a length of 3 meters is fixed at one end and free at the other. If the modulus of elasticity is 210 GPa and the moment of inertia is 2 × 10⁻⁶ m⁴, what is the critical buckling load?
   A) 720 N
   B) 960 N
   C) 1200 N
   D) 1440 N

9. A steel bar 1 meter long is heated from 20°C to 100°C. If the coefficient of thermal expansion is 12 × 10⁻⁶ /°C and the modulus of elasticity is 200 GPa, calculate the induced stress assuming no expansion is allowed.
   A) 192 MPa
   B) 200 MPa
   C) 210 MPa
   D) 240 MPa

10. A component is subjected to an alternating stress of 250 MPa with a mean stress of 150 MPa. What is the stress ratio R?
   A) 0.4
   B) -0.4
   C) 0.6
   D) -0.6

11. A material has a fracture toughness of 30 MPa√m. If a crack length of 10 mm is present, calculate the critical stress for fracture.
   A) 85 MPa
   B) 95 MPa
   C) 105 MPa
   D) 115 MPa

12. A cylindrical steel rod with Young’s modulus of 200 GPa is subjected to a tensile force of 10 kN. The rod has a diameter of 20 mm and a length of 1.5 m. What is the elongation of the rod?
   A) 0.375 mm
   B) 0.5 mm
   C) 0.75 mm
   D) 1.0 mm

13. A rectangular block of material is subjected to a shear force of 800 N. The block has a height of 10 cm, a width of 5 cm, and a shear modulus of 25 MPa. What is the shear strain?
   A) 0.0016 rad
   B) 0.0024 rad
   C) 0.0032 rad
   D) 0.0040 rad

14. A simply supported beam with a length of 4 m carries a uniformly distributed load of 10 kN/m. The beam’s Young’s modulus is 210 GPa, and its second moment of area is 80 × 10⁶ mm⁴. What is the maximum deflection of the beam?
   A) 10.2 mm
   B) 12.8 mm
   C) 14.7 mm
   D) 16.5 mm

15. A concrete column with a cross-sectional area of 0.3 m² supports an axial load of 500 kN. If the compressive strength of the concrete is 25 MPa, determine if the column is safe.
   A) Yes, the stress is below the compressive strength.
   B) No, the stress is above the compressive strength.
   C) Stress is equal to the compressive strength.
   D) Not enough data to determine.

16. A solid circular shaft with a diameter of 50 mm is subjected to a torque of 200 Nm. If the shear modulus of the material is 80 GPa, what is the angle of twist per meter length?
   A) 0.0004 rad
   B) 0.0011 rad
   C) 0.0016 rad
   D) 0.0023 rad

   A) 156 kN
   B) 200 kN
   C) 250 kN
   D) 300 kN

18. A steel rod of length 1 m is constrained at both ends and subjected to a temperature increase of 50°C. The coefficient of thermal expansion is 12 × 10⁻⁶ /°C, and Young’s modulus is 200 GPa. What is the thermal stress developed in the rod?
   A) 120 MPa
   B) 150 MPa
   C) 180 MPa
   D) 200 MPa

   C) 85 MPa
   D) 90 MPa

105. A material has a Young's modulus of 210 GPa and Poisson's ratio of 0.3. Calculate the material's shear modulus.
   A) 80.77 GPa
   B) 77.78 GPa
   C) 70.00 GPa
   D) 60.00 GPa

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Use the formula ΔL = (F * L) / (E * A), where A = π * d² / 4. Substituting values, ΔL = (40,000 * 2) / (200 * 10⁹ * π * (0.02)² / 4) = 0.4 mm.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Strain (ε) = Stress (σ) / Elastic Modulus (E). ε = 100 × 10⁶ / 210 × 10⁹ = 0.000476.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Use the torsion formula τ = T * r / J. J = π * d⁴ / 32 for a circular shaft. Rearrange to solve for d, and d = 31.2 mm.

4. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For a UDL over a simply supported beam, maximum bending moment = wL² / 8. Substituting values, M = (2 * 6²) / 8 = 18 kNm.

5. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Maximum principal stress is given by σ₁ = (σₓ + σᵧ) / 2 + √[((σₓ - σᵧ) / 2)² + τ²]. Substituting values gives σ₁ = 160 MPa.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Radius of Mohr's circle = √[((σₓ - σᵧ) / 2)² + τ²]. Substituting values, radius = √[0² + 30²] = 30 MPa.

7. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Deflection at free end of cantilever beam = (P * L³) / (3 * EI). Substituting values, δ = (500 * 4³) / (3 * 1 × 10⁶) = 16 mm.

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Critical load P = (π²EI) / (KL)². For fixed-free, K = 2. Substituting values, P = (π² * 210 * 10⁹ * 2 × 10⁻⁶) / (2 * 3)² = 960 N.

9. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal stress = E * α * ΔT. Substituting values, σ = 200 × 10⁹ * 12 × 10⁻⁶ * (100 - 20) = 192 MPa.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress ratio R = σₘᵢₙ / σₘₐₓ. For alternating stress, σₐ = (σₘₐₓ - σₘᵢₙ) / 2 and mean stress σₘ = (σₘₐₓ + σₘᵢₙ) / 2. Solving gives R = -0.4.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Critical stress σ = K₁c / √(πa). Substituting values, σ = 30 / √(π * 0.01) = 95 MPa.

12. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The elongation is calculated using the formula δ = (F × L) / (A × E). Substituting the given values: δ = (10 × 10³ × 1.5) / [(π * (0.02)² / 4) × 200 × 10⁹] = 0.375 mm.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The shear strain is calculated using γ = τ / G. First, calculate the shear stress: τ = F / A = 800 / (0.1 × 0.05) = 160 kPa. Then use γ = τ / G = 160 × 10³ / 25 × 10⁶ = 0.0016 rad.

14. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The formula for maximum deflection under a uniformly distributed load is δ_max = (5 × w × L⁴) / (384 × E × I). Substituting: δ_max = (5 × 10 × 4⁴) / (384 × 210 × 10⁹ × 80 × 10⁻⁶) = 12.8 mm.

15. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Stress = P / A = 500 × 10³ / 0.3 = 1.67 MPa. Since the stress (1.67 MPa) is below the compressive strength (25 MPa), the column is safe.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The angle of twist per unit length is θ/L = (T × L)/(J × G). First, calculate polar moment of inertia: J = π × d⁴ / 32 = π × (0.05)⁴ / 32 = 3.07 × 10⁻⁷ m⁴. Then θ/L = 200 / (3.07 × 10⁻⁷ × 80 × 10⁹) = 0.0016 rad.

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The critical buckling load is P_cr = (π² × E × I_min) / L². I_min = (1/12) × b × h³ = (1/12) × 0.05 × (0.1)³ = 4.17 × 10⁻⁷ m⁴. Substituting: P_cr = (π² × 200 × 10⁹ × 4.17 × 10⁻⁷) / 2² = 156 kN.

18. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Thermal stress is given by σ = α × E × ΔT. Substituting: σ = 12 × 10⁻⁶ × 200 × 10⁹ × 50 = 180 MPa.

19. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum stress = σ_axial + σ_bending. σ_axial = P / A = 30 × 10³ / (0.12 × 0.06) = 4.17 MPa. σ_bending = M × c / I = (5 × 10³ × 0.03) / [(1/12) × 0.12 × (0.06)³] = 6.93 MPa. Total stress = 4.17 + 6.93 = 11.1 MPa.

20. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Principal stresses are calculated using σ₁,₂ = [(σ_x + σ_y)/2] ± √[((σ_x − σ_y)/2)² + τ_xy²]. Substituting: σ₁ = 50 MPa, σ₂ = 15 MPa.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Stress amplitude = (σ_max − σ_min)/2 = (400 − 100)/2 = 150 MPa. Since 150 MPa > endurance limit (250 MPa), the material is not safe.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The shear strain at the outer surface is calculated using the relationship between torque, polar moment of inertia, and shear stress. The strain is then derived using shear modulus and stress.

23. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The maximum bending stress is calculated using the formula σ = M*c/I. The moment of inertia I is determined for the rectangular section, and c is the maximum distance to the outer fiber.

24. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Compressive stress is calculated using the formula σ = F/A, where A is the cross-sectional area of the specimen and F is the applied axial force.

25. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The centroid is calculated using the weighted average of the areas’ centroidal distances from the base. The symmetrical property simplifies calculations along the vertical axis.

26. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hoop stress is calculated using the formula σ_h = (p*d)/(2*t), where p is the pressure, d is the diameter, and t is the thickness of the pipe wall.

27. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Deflection at the free end is calculated using the cantilever beam deflection formula δ = (F*L^3)/(3*E*I). The moment of inertia I is based on the rectangular cross-section.

28. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The applied tensile force is determined using the formula F = (E*A*ΔL)/L, where ΔL is the elongation and L is the original length.

29. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Under equal deformation, the stress ratio is inversely proportional to the ratio of Young’s modulus multiplied by the cross-sectional area for each material.

30. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress in a biaxial stress state is given by τ_max = |(σ_x - σ_y)/2|.

31. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Longitudinal stress for a thin-walled cylinder is calculated using σ_l = (p*d)/(4*t).

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Axial stress is calculated using the formula σ = F/A. Substituting F = 5000 N and A = 10 × 10⁻⁶ m², σ = 5000 / 10 × 10⁻⁶ = 50 MPa.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The deflection for a cantilever beam under uniformly distributed load is Δ = (wL⁴)/(8EI). Substituting w = 2000 N/m, L = 2 m, EI = 1 × 10⁶ N·m², Δ = (2000 × 2⁴) / (8 × 1 × 10⁶) = 16 mm.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress τ = T*r/J. For a solid shaft, J = π*d⁴/32. Substituting T = 300 Nm, d = 75 mm, τ = 300 × (37.5 × 10⁻³) / (π × (75 × 10⁻³)⁴ / 32) = 11.3 MPa.

35. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Critical buckling load P_cr = (π²EI)/(L²). Substituting E = 210 × 10⁹ Pa, I = π*d⁴/64 (d = 50 mm), L = 3 m, P_cr = (π² × 210 × 10⁹ × π × (50 × 10⁻³)⁴ / 64) / (3²) = 19.4 kN.

36. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal stress is calculated using σ = EαΔT. Substituting E = 200 × 10⁹, α = 12 × 10⁻⁶, ΔT = 60, σ = 200 × 10⁹ × 12 × 10⁻⁶ × 60 = 120 MPa.

37. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress τ_max = √[(σ_x - σ_y)²/4 + τ_xy²]. Substituting the values, τ_max = √[(60 - (-40))²/4 + 30²] = √[100²/4 + 900] = 80 MPa.

38. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Normal stress due to bending σ_b = M*y/I and axial stress σ_a = F/A. Maximum stress = σ_b + σ_a. Substituting M = 5 × 10³ Nm, F = 10 × 10³ N, I = (100 × 200³)/12, A = 100 × 200, σ_b = 40 MPa, σ_a = 0.5 MPa, Total = 40 MPa.

39. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Strain ε = stress / E. Stress = F/A = 6000 / (π × (15 × 10⁻³)² / 4). Substituting E = 70 × 10⁹, ε = stress / E = 0.00057.

40. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Stress amplitude = (σ_max - σ_min) / 2. Substituting σ_max = 400 MPa, σ_min = 50 MPa, Stress amplitude = (400 - 50) / 2 = 150 MPa.

41. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Hoop stress σ_h = (P*r)/t. Substituting P = 2 × 10⁶ Pa, r = 1 m, t = 12 × 10⁻³ m, σ_h = (2 × 10⁶ × 1) / (12 × 10⁻³) = 166.7 MPa.

42. Correct Answer: A

   Explanation: Steel typically exhibits the highest toughness due to its ability to absorb energy and deform plastically under dynamic loading.

82. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Elongation is calculated using δ = (F * L) / (E * A). Here, A = π * (d/2)^2 = π * (0.02/2)^2 = 3.14 * 0.01^2 = 3.14 * 0.0001 = 0.000314 m². Substituting values: δ = (10,000 * 2) / (200,000,000 * 0.000314) = 0.0005 m = 0.50 mm.

83. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress in a rectangular cross-section is τ_max = 1.5 * V / Area. Here, Area = width * height = 0.1 * 0.3 = 0.03 m². τ_max = 1.5 * (50,000 / 0.03) = 3.33 MPa.

84. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Axial deformation is calculated using δ = (F * L) / (E * A). δ = (500,000 * 3) / (25,000,000 * 0.04) = 0.015 m = 0.150 mm.

85. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress is calculated as τ_max = √(((σ_x - σ_y)/2)^2 + τ_xy^2). τ_max = √(((80 - 50)/2)^2 + 30^2) = √(15^2 + 30^2) = √(225 + 900) = √1125 = 40 MPa.

86. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for UDL is given by δ_max = (5 * w * L^4) / (384 * E * I). Substituting: δ_max = (5 * 5000 * 4^4) / (384 * 200,000,000 * 8 * 10^-6) = 0.005 m = 5 mm.

87. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress for a circular shaft is given by τ_max = T*r/J. Here, the polar moment of inertia for a circular cross-section is J = π*r^4/2 = π*0.05^4/2 = 1.96x10^-6 m^4. τ_max = (500*0.05)/1.96x10^-6 = 40 MPa.

88. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The bending moment at the fixed end is M = P * L = 6 kN * 3 m = 18 kNm. The maximum bending stress is calculated as σ = M * c / I, where c = h/2 = 50 mm = 0.05 m and I = (b * h^3) / 12 = (0.05 m * (0.1 m)^3) / 12 = 4.167 × 10^-6 m^4. Substituting values, σ = (18 × 10^3 Nm) * 0.05 m / 4.167 × 10^-6 m^4 = 72 MPa.

89. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The hoop stress in a thin-walled pressure vessel is given by σ_h = (P * r) / t, where P = 2 MPa, r = 0.3 m, and t = 10 mm = 0.01 m. Substituting values, σ_h = (2 × 10^6 Pa * 0.3 m) / 0.01 m = 60 MPa.

90. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum shear stress is determined using τ_max = (σ_1 - σ_2) / 2, where σ_1 = 200 MPa and σ_2 = -100 MPa. Substituting, τ_max = (200 - (-100)) / 2 = 300 / 2 = 100 MPa.

91. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The deflection at the midpoint for a simply supported beam with a point load is δ = (P * L^3) / (48 * E * I), where I = (b * h^3) / 12 = (0.1 * (0.2)^3) / 12 = 6.67 × 10^-6 m^4. Substituting values, δ = (10 × 10^3 * (6)^3) / (48 * 200 × 10^9 * 6.67 × 10^-6) = 2.08 mm.

92. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Shear stress is calculated as τ = G * γ, where G = 80 GPa = 80 × 10^9 Pa and γ = 0.005 rad. Substituting values, τ = 80 × 10^9 * 0.005 = 200 MPa.

93. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The deformation for each section is δ = (P * L) / (A * E). For aluminum: δ_Al = (100 × 10^3 * 3) / (500 × 10^-6 * 70 × 10^9) = 8.57 × 10^-4 m. For steel: δ_Steel = (100 × 10^3 * 2) / (500 × 10^-6 * 200 × 10^9) = 2 × 10^-4 m. Total deformation is δ_total = δ_Al + δ_Steel = 1.07 × 10^-3 m = 2.14 mm.

94. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The normal stress is calculated using the formula: σ = P/A. The cross-sectional area of the circular rod is A = π(d^2)/4 = π(0.02^2)/4 = 3.14 × 10^-4 m². Substituting P = 50 kN, σ = 50,000 N / (3.14 × 10^-4 m²) = 79.57 MPa.

95. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Strain energy is calculated using the formula U = (1/2) × P × δ. Substituting P = 100,000 N and δ = 0.5 × 10^-3 m, U = (1/2) × 100,000 × 0.0005 = 25 J. However, considering the volume and modulus, strain energy further reduces to approximately 14.28 J.

96. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Maximum bending stress is calculated using the formula σ = (M × c) / I. The moment at the fixed end is M = P × L = 1,000 × 2 = 2,000 Nm. c = h/2 = 0.05 m. I = (b × h^3) / 12 = (0.05 × 0.1^3) / 12 = 4.167 × 10^-7 m^4. Substituting values, σ = (2000 × 0.05) / (4.167 × 10^-7) = 90 MPa.

97. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Shear stress (τ) is calculated using τ = V/A. The cross-sectional area A = thickness × width = 0.005 × 0.1 = 0.0005 m². Substituting V = 2,000 N, τ = 2,000 / 0.0005 = 40 MPa.

98. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The maximum shear stress is calculated using τ = T × r / J. The polar moment of inertia J = (π × d^4) / 32 = (π × 0.04^4) / 32 = 2.513 × 10^-8 m^4. r = d/2 = 0.02 m. Substituting values, τ = (300 × 0.02) / (2.513 × 10^-8) = 29.29 MPa.

99. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum deflection for a uniformly loaded simply supported beam is δ = (5 × w × L^4) / (384 × E × I). Substituting w = 1,000 N/m, L = 3 m, E = 200 × 10^9 Pa, and I = 100 × 10^-6 m^4, δ = (5 × 1,000 × 3^4) / (384 × 200 × 10^9 × 100 × 10^-6) = 0.052 mm.

100. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Axial stress is σ_axial = P/A = 10,000 / (0.08 × 0.12) = 10.42 MPa. Bending stress is σ_bending = (M × c) / I = (500 × 0.06) / [(0.08 × 0.12^3) / 12] = 19.58 MPa. Combined stress = σ_axial + σ_bending = 10.42 + 19.58 = 30 MPa.

101. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Critical buckling load is calculated using P_cr = (π^2 × E × I) / (K × L)^2. For fixed-free column, K = 2. Moment of inertia I = (b × d^3) / 12 = (0.05 × 0.2^3) / 12 = 3.333 × 10^-6 m^4. Substituting values, P_cr = [(π^2 × 200 × 10^9 × 3.333 × 10^-6) / (2 × 3)^2] = 31.42 kN.

102. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Thermal stress is calculated using σ = α × ΔT × E. Substituting α = 12 × 10^-6 /°C, ΔT = 50°C, and E = 200 × 10^9 Pa, σ = 12 × 10^-6 × 50 × 200 × 10^9 = 240 MPa.

103. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the Goodman relation, combined stress = mean stress + alternating stress = 150 + 100 = 250 MPa. Since this equals the endurance limit, the component will not fail.

104. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum principal stress is calculated using σ_1 = [(σ_x + σ_y)/2] + √[((σ_x - σ_y)/2)^2 + τ_xy^2]. Substituting values, σ_1 = [(60 + 30)/2] + √[((60 - 30)/2)^2 + 15^2] = 80 MPa.

105. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Shear modulus G is calculated using G = E / [2(1 + ν)]. Substituting E = 210 × 10^9 Pa and ν = 0.3, G = 210 × 10^9 / [2(1 + 0.3)] = 77.78 GPa.

   B) Toughness
   C) Strength
   D) Hardness

   B) Extrusion
   C) Casting

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Fluid Mechanics

1. A vertical cylindrical tank is filled with water up to a height of 10 meters. What is the pressure at the bottom of the tank due to the water? Assume the density of water is 1000 kg/m³ and acceleration due to gravity is 9.81 m/s².
   A) 98.1 kPa
   B) 100 kPa
   C) 101.3 kPa
   D) 120 kPa

2. Water flows through a horizontal pipe with a varying diameter. The velocity of water at the larger diameter section is 3 m/s, and the diameter there is 0.5 m. What is the velocity of water at a smaller section where the diameter is 0.25 m?
   A) 6 m/s
   B) 12 m/s
   C) 24 m/s
   D) 48 m/s

3. A fluid flows through a pipe with a reduction in elevation by 5 meters. If the velocity at the upper section is 10 m/s and pressure is 150 kPa, what is the pressure at the lower section assuming negligible friction losses?
   A) 199.05 kPa
   B) 200 kPa
   C) 100 kPa
   D) 250 kPa

4. A fluid with viscosity 0.001 Pa·s and density 1000 kg/m³ flows with velocity 2 m/s through a pipe of diameter 0.05 m. What is the Reynolds number of the flow?
   A) 100
   B) 4000
   C) 10,000
   D) 2000

5. Water flows through a pipe with a roughness coefficient of 0.02. If the length of the pipe is 50 meters and the velocity is 3 m/s, how much head loss occurs due to friction? Assume diameter is 0.1 m and use Darcy-Weisbach equation.
   A) 2.92 m
   B) 3.45 m
   C) 4.62 m
   D) 5.89 m

6. A pump delivers water at a rate of 0.05 m³/s through a pipe with a diameter of 0.2 m. What is the average velocity of water in the pipe?
   A) 1.59 m/s
   B) 2.12 m/s
   C) 3.18 m/s
   D) 5.00 m/s

7. A solid cylindrical object is submerged in water. If its weight is 100 N and the buoyant force is 80 N, what is the net force acting on the object?
   A) 20 N upward
   B) 20 N downward
   C) 80 N upward
   D) 100 N downward

8. Which of the following fluids has the highest dynamic viscosity at room temperature?
   A) Water
   B) Air
   C) Honey
   D) Oil

   A) Orifice plate
   B) Pitot tube
   C) Venturi meter
   D) All of the above

10. What is the Mach number for a fluid traveling at 340 m/s in an environment where the speed of sound is 300 m/s?
   A) 0.88
   B) 1.13
   C) 3.00
   D) 0.50

11. A rectangular tank is filled with water and has a movable vertical wall. The wall has a height of 2 meters and a width of 1 meter. What is the total force exerted by the water on the wall when the tank is filled to the brim?
   A) 9,800 N
   B) 19,600 N
   C) 3,920 N
   D) 7,840 N

12. Water flows through a pipe with a varying cross-section. The diameter at point A is 0.1 m, and the diameter at point B is 0.05 m. If the velocity at point A is 2 m/s, what is the velocity at point B?
   A) 4 m/s
   B) 8 m/s
   C) 16 m/s
   D) 2 m/s

13. A fluid has a dynamic viscosity of 0.001 Pa·s and a density of 1000 kg/m³. What is its kinematic viscosity?
   A) 1 × 10⁻⁶ m²/s
   B) 1 × 10⁻³ m²/s
   C) 1 × 10⁻² m²/s
   D) 1 × 10⁻⁵ m²/s

14. A horizontal pipeline has water flowing through it. At one section, the pressure is 120 kPa and the velocity is 3 m/s. At another section, the velocity is 6 m/s. What is the pressure at the second section, ignoring friction losses?
   A) 90 kPa
   B) 105 kPa
   C) 75 kPa
   D) 120 kPa

   B) 25,000
   C) 5,000

   C) 2 m/s
   D) 0.5 m/s

   B) 12.26 kW
   C) 6.67 kW
   D) 10.21 kW

124. A jet of water strikes a stationary flat plate vertically with a velocity of 8 m/s and a flow rate of 0.1 m³/s. What is the force exerted by the water on the plate?
   A) 800 N
   B) 400 N
   C) 640 N
   D) 1020 N

125. Which of the following best represents a situation where the flow is critical?
   A) Mach number = 1
   B) Froude number = 1
   C) Reynolds number = 4000
   D) Weber number = 1

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The pressure due to a liquid column is calculated using P = ρgh. Substituting values: P = (1000 kg/m³)(9.81 m/s²)(10 m) = 98,100 Pa = 98.1 kPa.

2. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the continuity equation: A1V1 = A2V2. With A = πd²/4, A1 = π(0.5)²/4, A2 = π(0.25)²/4. Solving for V2: V2 = V1(A1/A2) = 3 m/s × [(0.5²)/(0.25²)] = 12 m/s.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using Bernoulli's equation: P1 + ρgh1 + 0.5ρv1² = P2 + ρgh2 + 0.5ρv2². Substitute values, rearrange for P2, and calculate: P2 = P1 + ρg(h1-h2).

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Reynolds number is calculated as Re = (ρVD)/μ. Substituting values: Re = (1000)(2)(0.05)/(0.001) = 4000.

5. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Darcy-Weisbach equation: hf = f(L/D)(v²/2g). Calculate f using empirical methods or given directly, then substitute into the equation.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Average velocity can be calculated using Q = A × V → V = Q/A. A = πd²/4.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Net force = Weight - Buoyant force. Here, net force = 100 N - 80 N = 20 N downward.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Honey has significantly higher viscosity compared to water, air, and oil at room temperature.

9. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: All listed devices measure flow based on pressure differences caused by changes in velocity and area.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Mach number is calculated as M = V/a, where V is the velocity and a is the speed of sound. M = 340/300 = 1.13.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The force exerted by the water on the wall is calculated using pressure distribution. Pressure at the bottom is ρgh = 1000 * 9.8 * 2 = 19,600 Pa. Since pressure varies linearly, the average pressure is 9,800 Pa. The area of the wall is 2 * 1 = 2 m². Total force = Average Pressure * Area = 9,800 * 2 = 19,600 N.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the continuity equation A₁v₁ = A₂v₂. The area at A is π(0.1/2)² = 0.00785 m², and the area at B is π(0.05/2)² = 0.00196 m². Solving 0.00785 * 2 = 0.00196 * v₂ yields v₂ = 8 m/s.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Kinematic viscosity ν = μ / ρ. Given μ = 0.001 Pa·s and ρ = 1000 kg/m³, ν = 0.001 / 1000 = 1 × 10⁻³ m²/s.

14. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Using Bernoulli's principle: P₁ + (1/2)ρv₁² = P₂ + (1/2)ρv₂². Substituting, 120,000 + 0.5 * 1000 * 3² = P₂ + 0.5 * 1000 * 6². Solving yields P₂ = 75,000 Pa or 75 kPa.

15. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Re = ρvd/μ. Substituting values: Re = (0.5 × 0.1) / (1 × 10⁻⁶) = 5,000. Laminar flow typically occurs for Re < 2,300.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Orifice meters typically measure turbulent flow effectively due to significant pressure drops and high Reynolds numbers.

17. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Flow rate Q = A × v. The cross-sectional area is 2 × 1 = 2 m². Q = 2 × 1.5 = 3 m³/s.

18. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Efficiency = (Output Power / Input Power) × 100. Output Power = Qρgh = (10/3600)×1000×9.8×10 = 2.72 kW. Efficiency = (2.72 / 5) × 100 ≈ 78%.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Hydrostatic force is derived using pressure distribution. The average depth is ρgh = 1000×9.8×1 = 9,800 Pa. Area = π×r²/2 = 6.28 m². Force = pressure × area = 9,800 × 6.28 = 39,200 N.

20. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Boundary layer separation occurs when an adverse pressure gradient forces fluid particles to decelerate, causing flow reversal.

21. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Kinematic viscosity is defined as the dynamic viscosity divided by the density. (ν = μ / ρ). Substituting the values: ν = 0.02 / 850 = 0.0000235 m²/s = 23.5 mm²/s.

22. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Pressure in a static fluid is calculated using the formula P = ρgh. Substituting the values: P = (1000)(9.81)(3) = 29430 Pa = 29.43 kPa.

23. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the continuity equation A₁V₁ = A₂V₂. Area is proportional to diameter squared. For A₁V₁ = A₂V₂: (π/4)(0.5²)(2) = (π/4)(0.25²)(V₂). Solving for V₂ gives 8 m/s.

24. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Bernoulli’s equation states that total energy remains constant along a streamline. An increase in elevation increases potential energy while keeping total energy unchanged.

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For laminar flow, the average velocity is half the maximum velocity (V_avg = V_max / 2). Average velocity = 0.3 / 2 = 0.15 m/s.

26. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Re = ρVD/μ. Substituting the given values: Re = (1000)(2)(0.05)/(0.001) = 5000.

27. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Head loss is calculated as h_f = f(L/D)(V²/(2g)). Substituting: h_f = 0.02(100/0.25)(1²/(2×9.81)) ≈ 2 m.

28. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The energy grade line represents total energy per unit weight, which remains constant in a steady flow assuming no energy losses.

29. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Flow rate Q = A × V, where A is the cross-sectional area. Doubling the depth doubles the area, thereby doubling the flow rate.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Power required = ρgQh. Substituting: Power = (1000)(9.81)(0.05)(20) = 19.62 kW.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the principle of continuity (A1V1 = A2V2), the velocity in the smaller section can be calculated as 4 m/s.

32. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The cube displaces water equal to its weight. Calculating the buoyant force and comparing densities, 2/3 of the cube will be submerged.

33. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Pressure difference is calculated using ΔP = ρgh. For mercury, ρ = 13600 kg/m³, g = 9.81 m/s², and h = 0.2 m.

34. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: According to Bernoulli's equation, pressure decreases as velocity increases in the smaller section.

35. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The wetted perimeter is calculated as the sum of the bottom width and the sloping sides: WP = 2 + 2√(1² + 1.5²).

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Reynolds number is calculated using Re = (ρVD)/μ or V*D/ν. Substituting the values gives Re = 10000.

37. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the energy equation, head loss can be calculated as h = P/(ρgQ). Substituting gives h = 10.2 m.

38. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the principle of continuity (Q_total = A_total * V_total), the velocity in the merged pipe is calculated as 1.25 m/s.

39. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For isentropic processes, T2/T1 = (P2/P1)^(γ-1/γ). Substituting values and γ=1.4 gives T2 = 540 K.

40. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using Bernoulli’s equation and continuity, the flow rate is calculated considering the pressure difference and area ratio.

41. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The kinematic viscosity is calculated by dividing dynamic viscosity by density: ν = μ / ρ = 0.001 / 1000 = 0.0001 m²/s.

42. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The pressure due to the water column is calculated using P = ρgh. With ρ = 1000 kg/m³, g = 9.81 m/s², h = 5 m, the pressure due to the water is 1000 * 9.81 * 5 = 49,050 Pa or 49.05 kPa. Adding atmospheric pressure gives 150.3 kPa.

43. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using the principle of continuity, A₁V₁ = A₂V₂. With A₁ = π(0.2/2)², A₂ = π(0.1/2)², and V₁ = 2, solving gives V₂ = 4 m/s.

44. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Using Bernoulli’s equation: P₁ + 0.5ρV₁² = P₂ + 0.5ρV₂². With ρ = 1000 kg/m³, solving gives P₂ = 200 - 0.5 * 1000 * (3² - 1²) = 183 kPa.

45. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Re = VD / ν = (2 * 0.05) / (1 × 10⁻⁶) = 10,000.

46. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: According to Bernoulli's principle, a decrease in pressure corresponds to an increase in velocity in the constricted throat of the Venturi meter.

47. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: An increased angle of attack generally results in increased drag due to greater turbulence and separation of flow.

48. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Mach number is the ratio of flow velocity to the speed of sound and is used to characterize compressible flows.

49. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Friction between the fluid and the pipe walls is the primary cause of head loss in pipe flows.

50. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: A transitional boundary layer occurs when laminar flow transitions into turbulent flow.

51. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The hydraulic radius is calculated as the cross-sectional area divided by the wetted perimeter: R = (width * depth) / (width + 2 * depth) = 2 * 1 / (2 + 2) = 0.5 m.

52. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Supersonic flow occurs when Mach > 1.

53. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Wake formation is influenced by the Reynolds number, which characterizes flow behavior around objects.

54. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: According to Archimedes' principle, the buoyant force equals the weight of the displaced fluid.

55. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A centrifugal pump uses rotational energy from a motor to increase the fluid's energy.

56. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Laminar flow is characterized by smooth and parallel streamlines.

57. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The continuity equation ensures that mass flow rate remains constant within a closed pipe network.

58. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The energy grade line represents the total energy (pressure, velocity, and elevation) per unit weight of the fluid.

59. Correct Answer: B

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Thermodynamics

1. A rigid, insulated tank is divided into two compartments. One contains gas at 2 MPa and the other is evacuated. If the partition is removed, allowing the gas to fill the entire tank, what will be the final pressure of the gas?
   A) The final pressure will be less than 2 MPa.
   B) The final pressure will be more than 2 MPa.
   C) The final pressure will remain at 2 MPa.
   D) The final pressure depends on the initial temperature.

2. A heat engine operates between a heat source at 600 K and a heat sink at 300 K. What is the maximum possible thermal efficiency of the engine?
   A) 50%
   B) 25%
   C) 66.7%
   D) 33.3%

3. Water is heated at constant pressure from a saturated liquid state. At what point will it become a saturated vapor?
   A) At the boiling point of water at the given pressure
   B) At 100°C
   C) At the critical temperature
   D) When the enthalpy reaches its minimum

4. In an ideal Rankine cycle, what is the purpose of the condenser?
   A) To increase the pressure of the steam
   B) To convert steam into liquid water
   C) To superheat the steam
   D) To extract work from the steam

5. In an ideal Brayton cycle, which process occurs in the compressor?
   A) Isentropic compression
   B) Isobaric expansion
   C) Isothermal compression
   D) Adiabatic expansion

6. A metal rod is subjected to a temperature gradient. Which form of heat transfer primarily occurs within the rod?
   A) Conduction
   B) Convection
   C) Radiation
   D) Advection

7. What property of air increases when water is evaporated into it at constant pressure?
   A) Dry bulb temperature
   B) Humidity ratio
   C) Specific volume decreases
   D) Enthalpy decreases

8. A refrigerator has a coefficient of performance (COP) of 5. If the work input is 2 kW, what is the refrigeration effect?
   A) 10 kW
   B) 5 kW
   C) 2 kW
   D) 8 kW

9. What happens to the entropy of the universe during an irreversible process in an isolated system?
   A) Entropy decreases
   B) Entropy remains constant
   C) Entropy increases
   D) Entropy can either increase or decrease

10. A heat exchanger is designed to transfer heat from hot water at 80°C to cold water at 20°C. Which configuration will maximize the rate of heat transfer?
   A) Parallel flow
   B) Counterflow
   C) Crossflow
   D) Concentric flow

11. What is the primary purpose of an intercooler in a multi-stage compressor?
   A) To increase the temperature of the compressed air
   B) To decrease the work input required
   C) To increase the final pressure of the air
   D) To increase the volumetric efficiency of the compressor

12. A piston-cylinder device contains air at 300 K and 100 kPa. The air is compressed isothermally to 400 kPa. What is the change in entropy of the system?
   A) -0.287 kJ/K
   B) 0 kJ/K
   C) 0.287 kJ/K
   D) 0.574 kJ/K

13. Steam at 2 MPa and 300°C passes through a nozzle. If the steam velocity at the inlet is negligible and the exit velocity is 400 m/s, what is the change in enthalpy of the steam?
   A) 80 kJ/kg
   B) 160 kJ/kg
   C) 320 kJ/kg
   D) 640 kJ/kg

14. In an ideal Otto cycle, the compression ratio is 10. If the specific heat ratio (γ) is 1.4, what is the thermal efficiency of the cycle?
   A) 47.5%
   B) 53.8%
   C) 60.2%
   D) 75.0%

15. A flat plate is maintained at a constant temperature of 100°C while air at 25°C flows past it. If the convection heat transfer coefficient is 25 W/m²·K, what is the heat flux?
   A) 625 W/m²
   B) 1875 W/m²
   C) 2500 W/m²
   D) 3750 W/m²

16. A Carnot engine operates between a hot reservoir at 500 K and a cold reservoir at 300 K. If the engine receives 900 kJ of heat from the hot reservoir, how much work does it produce?
   A) 360 kJ
   B) 540 kJ
   C) 720 kJ
   D) 900 kJ

17. A closed system undergoes a polytropic process where PV^1.2 = constant. If the initial pressure and volume are 150 kPa and 0.1 m³, and the final volume is 0.05 m³, what is the final pressure?
   A) 450 kPa
   B) 600 kPa
   C) 750 kPa
   D) 900 kPa

   A) 41.7%
   B) 50.0%

   C) 3.57 kW

51. What is the primary difference between an open system and a closed system?

99. In a Rankine cycle, steam exits the turbine at 100 kPa with a quality of 0.85 and enters the condenser. What is the significance of the quality in this context?
   A) It determines the pressure drop in the condenser.
   B) It represents the fraction of the steam that is liquid.
   C) It determines the efficiency of the turbine.
   D) It represents the fraction of the steam that is vapor.
   correct_answer) D
   explanation) The quality of the steam indicates the proportion of vapor phase in the mixture, which is critical for determining the energy content and phase changes.

159. In an ideal vapor-compression refrigeration cycle, what is the main function of the throttle valve?
   A) Increase the temperature of the refrigerant
   B) Lower the pressure and temperature of the refrigerant
   C) Remove latent heat from the refrigerant
   D) Compress the refrigerant
   correct_answer) B
   explanation) The throttle valve in a refrigeration cycle is used to lower the refrigerant’s pressure and temperature through an isenthalpic (constant enthalpy) expansion process.
