175. In an actual Rankine cycle, the enthalpy of steam entering the turbine is 3200 kJ/kg, and the enthalpy of steam exiting the turbine is 2100 kJ/kg. If the pump work is negligible, what is the thermal efficiency of the cycle if the enthalpy of the steam exiting the condenser is 900 kJ/kg?
   A) 25%
   B) 30%
   C) 40%
   D) 50%

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: When the gas expands into the evacuated compartment, its pressure will decrease because of the increase in volume, assuming the process is adiabatic.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum efficiency of a heat engine is given by the Carnot efficiency: 1 - (T_sink / T_source). Substituting the values: 1 - (300/600) = 0.5 or 50%.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Saturated vapor occurs when the water completely transitions from liquid at the boiling point temperature corresponding to the given pressure.

4. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The condenser converts exhaust steam from the turbine into liquid water, making it ready for compression in the pump.

5. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In the Brayton cycle, the compressor performs isentropic (adiabatic and reversible) compression to raise the pressure of the working fluid.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Heat transfer within a solid due to a temperature gradient occurs exclusively through conduction.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Evaporating water into air increases the humidity ratio, as the amount of water vapor in the air increases.

8. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The refrigeration effect is given by COP × work input. Substituting the values: 5 × 2 kW = 10 kW.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: In an irreversible process, the entropy of an isolated system always increases according to the second law of thermodynamics.

10. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Counterflow heat exchangers maximize the temperature difference across the length of the exchanger, increasing the rate of heat transfer.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: An intercooler reduces the temperature of the air between stages, thereby reducing the work required in subsequent compression stages.

12. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: In an isothermal process for an ideal gas, the change in entropy can be calculated using the formula ΔS = m*R*ln(P2/P1). Since air behaves as an ideal gas, the negative value indicates entropy decreases during compression.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Using the energy equation for steady flow, the change in enthalpy is derived from the kinetic energy term, Δh = v^2/2. Here, Δh = (400)^2 / (2*1000) = 160 kJ/kg.

14. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The efficiency of an Otto cycle is given by η = 1 - (1/r^(γ-1)), where r is the compression ratio and γ is the specific heat ratio. Substituting values, η = 1 - (1/10^(0.4)) ≈ 0.602 = 60.2%.

15. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Heat flux is calculated using q = h*(T_s - T_inf). Substituting values: q = 25*(100 - 25) = 625 W/m².

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The efficiency of a Carnot engine is η = 1 - (T_c/T_h). Substituting values: η = 1 - (300/500) = 0.4. Work output is W = η*Q_in = 0.4*900 = 360 kJ.

17. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For a polytropic process PV^n = constant. Solving for P2: P2 = P1*(V1/V2)^n = 150*(0.1/0.05)^1.2 ≈ 750 kPa.

18. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Efficiency is calculated as η = W_out/Q_in. Substituting values: η = 500/1200 = 0.417 = 41.7%.

19. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The latent heat of vaporization of water at atmospheric pressure (101.3 kPa) and 100°C is approximately 2257 kJ/kg, a standard thermophysical property.

20. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The COP of a heat pump is calculated as COP = T_hot/(T_hot - T_cold). Using T in Kelvin, COP = (293)/(293-268) ≈ 11.7. Q_out = COP*W = 11.7*2 ≈ 7.7 kW.

21. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For an insulated rigid tank, no heat transfer or work occurs, implying internal energy remains constant. Thus, temperature does not change.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: For an isentropic process of an ideal gas, T2/T1 = (P2/P1)^(γ-1/γ). Substituting the values (P2/P1 = 10, γ = 1.4, T1 = 300 K), T2 = 300 * (10)^(0.4/1.4) = 678 K.

23. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The maximum efficiency of the heat engine is given by η = 1 - (T_low / T_high) = 1 - (300/600) = 0.5. For heat rejected Q_L = 400 kJ, Q_H = Q_L / (1 - η) = 400 / 0.5 = 800 kJ. Work output W = Q_H - Q_L = 800 - 400 = 200 kJ.

24. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The condenser in a Rankine cycle rejects heat to the surroundings, causing the steam to condense into a liquid at constant pressure. This enables the pump to increase the liquid pressure efficiently in the next stage.

25. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The equation P(V - b) = RT is a modified ideal gas law that accounts for the finite volume of gas molecules (represented by b), which corresponds to intermolecular repulsion. It does not account for intermolecular attraction.

26. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: For an isothermal process, W = nRT ln(P1/P2). Using n = m/R_specific, where R_specific for air can be determined, and substituting the given values, the work done is 277.3 kJ.

27. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The rate of heat conduction is given by Fourier’s law, Q = kA(ΔT/L). Substituting the given values, Q = (385)(0.01)(373 - 273)/1 = 385 W.

28. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The entropy change of the high-temperature reservoir is ΔS_H = -Q_H/T_H. The entropy change of the low-temperature reservoir is ΔS_L = Q_L/T_L. Net entropy change is ΔS_net = ΔS_H + ΔS_L. Substituting the values, ΔS_net = -10/300 + 8/290 = 0.0167 kJ/K.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The critical point represents the maximum temperature and pressure at which a liquid and vapor phase can coexist. Beyond this point, the substance exists as a supercritical fluid, with no distinct phase boundaries.

30. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: According to the First Law of Thermodynamics, the change in internal energy (ΔU) equals the heat added to the system (Q) minus the work done by the system (W). ΔU = Q - W. Final internal energy = Initial internal energy + ΔU = 100 kJ + (50 kJ - 20 kJ) = 130 kJ.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a reversible isothermal process, entropy change is given by ΔS = Q/T, where Q is the heat transfer and T is the constant temperature during the process.

32. Correct Answer: D

172. Correct Answer: B

175. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Thermal efficiency for a Rankine cycle is η = (Wt - Qc) / Qh, where Wt = turbine work and Qh = heat added. Here, Wt = 3200 - 2100 = 1100 kJ/kg and Qc = 2100 - 900 = 1200 kJ/kg. Qh = heat added = 3200 - 900 = 2300 kJ/kg. Thus, η = (1100) / (2300) = 0.478, or approximately 40%.

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Heat Transfer

1. A steel rod (thermal conductivity k = 50 W/m·K) is exposed to a temperature difference of 100°C across its 2-meter length. If the cross-sectional area of the rod is 0.01 m², calculate the rate of heat transfer through the rod.
   A) 250 W
   B) 500 W
   C) 1,000 W
   D) 2,500 W

2. Water is flowing over a flat plate with a convective heat transfer coefficient of 150 W/m²·K. If the temperature difference between the surface and the water is 20°C, calculate the heat flux.
   A) 2,000 W/m²
   B) 3,000 W/m²
   C) 1,500 W/m²
   D) 750 W/m²

3. A surface with an emissivity of 0.8 has a temperature of 500 K and is radiating heat to surroundings at 300 K. What is the net radiative heat transfer rate per unit area? (Stefan-Boltzmann constant σ = 5.67 × 10⁻⁸ W/m²·K⁴)
   A) 1,224 W/m²
   B) 912 W/m²
   C) 1,000 W/m²
   D) 1,800 W/m²

4. A composite wall consists of two layers: Layer 1 (k = 0.5 W/m·K, thickness = 0.05 m) and Layer 2 (k = 1.0 W/m·K, thickness = 0.1 m). Calculate the overall thermal resistance per unit area.
   A) 0.3 m²·K/W
   B) 0.25 m²·K/W
   C) 0.2 m²·K/W
   D) 0.15 m²·K/W

5. A counterflow heat exchanger has hot fluid entering at 120°C and exiting at 80°C while cold fluid enters at 40°C and exits at 70°C. If the overall heat transfer coefficient is 250 W/m²·K and the heat transfer area is 10 m², calculate the rate of heat transfer. (Assume log mean temperature difference ΔTₘ = 40°C)
   A) 100,000 W
   B) 110,000 W
   C) 120,000 W
   D) 125,000 W

6. A metal sphere (density = 7,800 kg/m³, specific heat = 500 J/kg·K) initially at 500°C is cooled by air at 25°C. If the heat transfer coefficient is 50 W/m²·K and the sphere has a surface area of 0.1 m², calculate the time constant τ.
   A) 78 seconds
   B) 60 seconds
   C) 100 seconds
   D) 90 seconds

7. A rectangular fin with a thermal conductivity of 200 W/m·K has a thickness of 0.01 m, height of 0.05 m, and a base temperature of 100°C. If the surroundings are at 25°C and the convective heat transfer coefficient is 10 W/m²·K, calculate the heat loss per unit length of the fin.
   A) 75 W
   B) 50 W
   C) 100 W
   D) 125 W

8. A vertical plate is used for condensing steam at 100°C. The plate is maintained at 90°C. If the latent heat of vaporization for steam is 2,260 kJ/kg and the condensation rate is 0.01 kg/s, calculate the heat transfer rate.
   A) 22.6 kW
   B) 20 kW
   C) 25 kW
   D) 30 kW

9. A wall is insulated with material of thermal conductivity 0.04 W/m·K and thickness 0.1 m. If the temperature difference across the wall is 30°C, calculate the heat flux.
   A) 12 W/m²
   B) 15 W/m²
   C) 10 W/m²
   D) 8 W/m²

10. In a steady-state energy balance, a furnace transfers 1,000 W to a fluid stream. If 200 W is lost through radiation and 300 W through convection, how much heat is absorbed by the fluid?
   A) 500 W
   B) 600 W
   C) 800 W
   D) 1,000 W

11. A plane wall with a thermal conductivity of 2 W/m·K has thickness 0.2 m and is exposed to temperatures of 400°C on one side and 300°C on the other. What is the heat transfer rate per unit area through the wall?
   A) 500 W/m²
   B) 1000 W/m²
   C) 200 W/m²
   D) 600 W/m²

12. Air flows over a cylinder with a surface temperature of 400°C and ambient air at 50°C. The convective heat transfer coefficient is 25 W/m²·K. If the cylinder has a surface area of 2 m², what is the convective heat transfer rate?
   A) 17,500 W
   B) 35,000 W
   C) 22,500 W
   D) 25,000 W

13. A blackbody surface at 600 K radiates energy. If the Stefan-Boltzmann constant is 5.67 × 10^-8 W/m²·K⁴, what is the radiative heat flux emitted by the surface?
   A) 1,220 W/m²
   B) 22,680 W/m²
   C) 4,522 W/m²
   D) 9,720 W/m²

14. A parallel flow heat exchanger has hot water entering at 80°C and exiting at 60°C. Cold water enters at 30°C and exits at 50°C. What is the log mean temperature difference (LMTD) if the hot and cold fluids exchange heat uniformly?
   A) 27.7°C
   B) 22.4°C
   C) 25.0°C
   D) 20.3°C

15. A steel plate with density 7,800 kg/m³, specific heat 500 J/kg·K, and thickness 0.01 m is initially at 200°C. It is suddenly exposed to a convective environment at 50°C with a heat transfer coefficient of 100 W/m²·K. What is the Biot number for this system?
   A) 0.02
   B) 0.1
   C) 0.5
   D) 0.01

16. A long rod with thermal diffusivity α = 1 × 10^-5 m²/s and thermal conductivity k = 200 W/m·K has one end maintained at 500°C. Assuming steady-state heat conduction, how long does it take for a point 0.1 m from the heated end to reach 450°C?
   A) 50 s
   B) 500 s
   C) 1,000 s
   D) It never reaches steady-state

   A) 200 kW
   B) 50 kW
   C) 100 kW

   A) Constant temperature within the sphere
   B) Linear temperature gradient
   C) Radial temperature gradient
   D) Steady-state heat transfer
   correct_answer) A
   explanation) Since the Biot number is much less than 1, the internal conduction resistance is negligible compared to external convective resistance. Thus, assuming constant temperature within the sphere is valid.

123. A sphere of radius 0.1 m is initially at a uniform temperature of 300°C. It is suddenly exposed to an environment at 50°C. If the Biot number is 0.05, which assumption is valid for the analysis of the heat transfer?
   A) Heat transfer is steady-state.
   B) Lumped system analysis is applicable.
   C) Thermal resistance of the sphere is negligible.
   D) Convection dominates conduction.

124. A fin with a rectangular cross-section has a length of 10 cm, a thickness of 2 mm, and a thermal conductivity of 200 W/m·K. If the heat transfer coefficient on the surface is 100 W/m²·K, what is the fin efficiency?
   A) 55%
   B) 72%
   C) 85%
   D) 90%

125. A composite slab consists of a steel layer (k = 50 W/m·K) and an aluminum layer (k = 200 W/m·K). Each layer is 10 mm thick. Air flows over the aluminum surface with h = 25 W/m²·K. If the temperature difference across the slab is 100°C, what is the overall heat transfer rate per unit area?
   A) 300 W/m²
   B) 400 W/m²
   C) 500 W/m²
   D) 600 W/m²

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The heat transfer rate via conduction is calculated using Fourier’s Law: Q = (k × A × ΔT) / L. Substituting the values: Q = (50 × 0.01 × 100) / 2 = 500 W.

2. Correct Answer: A

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Measurements, Instrumentation, and Controls

1. A pressure gauge is used to measure the pressure of a gas in a tank. The gauge reads 125 kPa. If the atmospheric pressure is 101 kPa, what is the absolute pressure of the gas in the tank?
   A) 24 kPa
   B) 125 kPa
   C) 226 kPa
   D) 101 kPa

2. Which of the following is an example of a primary transducer in a measurement system?
   A) Thermocouple
   B) Strain gauge
   C) Bourdon tube
   D) Digital display

3. In a proportional control system, increasing the proportional gain (Kp) typically results in:
   A) Higher steady-state error
   B) Faster response time but higher oscillations
   C) Lower system stability
   D) Constant system behavior

4. Which type of flow meter is best suited for measuring the flow rate of a viscous fluid?
   A) Orifice plate
   B) Venturi meter
   C) Rotameter
   D) Positive displacement meter

5. What is the purpose of the Wheatstone bridge in a strain gauge system?
   A) To amplify the signal
   B) To convert mechanical strain to electrical signal
   C) To measure impedance
   D) To measure temperature

6. What is the main advantage of PID control over pure proportional control?
   A) Improved steady-state error handling
   B) Faster system response
   C) Reduced complexity
   D) Lower cost

7. A thermistor is used to measure temperature. What happens to the resistance of a thermistor as temperature increases?
   A) Resistance increases
   B) Resistance decreases
   C) Resistance remains constant
   D) Resistance oscillates

8. Which type of sensor is commonly used for non-contact temperature measurement?
   A) Thermocouple
   B) Infrared sensor
   C) RTD
   D) Thermistor

9. In a feedback control system, the term 'dead time' refers to:
   A) The time required for the system to stabilize after disturbance
   B) The delay between input and output response
   C) The time when the system does not operate
   D) The time system operates without energy

10. Which of the following devices is used to measure angular velocity?
   A) Rheometer
   B) Gyroscope
   C) Tachometer
   D) Barometer

11. What is the function of a signal conditioner in a measurement system?
   A) To display the output
   B) To amplify and filter the signal
   C) To measure the input signal
   D) To provide power supply to the sensor

12. A system has a transfer function G(s) = 5/(s+2). What is the system's time constant?
   A) 5 seconds
   B) 2 seconds
   C) 0.5 seconds
   D) 0.2 seconds

13. What type of measuring instrument is used to determine the hardness of a material?
   A) Caliper
   B) Rockwell tester
   C) Micrometer
   D) Spectrum analyzer

14. Which of the following sensors is used to measure force?
   A) Strain gauge
   B) Thermistor

75. An engineer needs to measure the torque applied to a rotating shaft in a high-temperature environment. Which of the following measurement devices is most appropriate for this application?

   C) Capacitive proximity sensor

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Absolute pressure is the sum of gauge pressure and atmospheric pressure. Therefore, 125 kPa + 101 kPa = 226 kPa.

2. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: A Bourdon tube is a primary transducer that converts pressure into mechanical displacement, which can then be measured.

3. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Increasing proportional gain improves response time but can lead to increased oscillations and overshoot.

4. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Positive displacement meters are ideal for viscous fluids as they measure the actual volume displaced by the fluid.

5. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The Wheatstone bridge is used to convert the small changes in resistance due to strain into measurable electrical signals.

6. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: PID control reduces steady-state error by incorporating integral and derivative components along with proportional control.

7. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Thermistors typically exhibit a decrease in resistance with an increase in temperature (negative temperature coefficient).

8. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Infrared sensors measure temperature without contact by detecting infrared radiation emitted by an object.

9. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Dead time is the delay between the application of an input and the start of the system's response.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: A tachometer is specifically designed to measure angular velocity or rotational speed.

11. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Signal conditioners process the raw sensor signal, often amplifying or filtering it to ensure compatibility with downstream components.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The time constant is the inverse of the coefficient of 's' in the denominator of the transfer function, which is 1/2 = 0.5 seconds.

13. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: A Rockwell tester measures the hardness of a material by determining the depth of penetration under a specific load.

14. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Strain gauges measure force indirectly by detecting the deformation of a material under load.

15. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Derivative control predicts future errors based on the rate of change of the current error, helping to improve system stability.

16. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Ultrasonic flow meters use the time of flight of sound waves in the fluid to measure flow rate.

17. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: RTDs are more accurate and stable than thermocouples but may have a slower response time.

18. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: An open-loop control system operates without feedback and relies on predefined inputs to control the output.

19. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Linear Variable Differential Transformers (LVDTs) are highly precise sensors used for displacement measurement.

20. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Piezoelectric sensors convert mechanical stress into electrical signals, making them ideal for dynamic pressure and vibration measurements.

21. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Type K thermocouples are commonly used for high-temperature environments like furnaces, and their output voltage corresponds to temperature ranges up to 1260°C.

22. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Digital flow meters generally provide higher accuracy and precision due to their ability to process signals electronically.

23. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: PID control combines proportional, integral, and derivative strategies to handle disturbances effectively while ensuring rapid response.

24. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The change in resistance can be calculated using the formula ΔR/R = GF × strain. Substituting GF = 2.1 and strain = 500 × 10^-6, the change in resistance is 1.05%.

25. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: RTDs (Resistance Temperature Detectors) are highly sensitive and provide precise temperature measurements due to their predictable resistance changes with temperature.

26. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: Gain margin is the amount by which a system's gain can be increased before it reaches the point of instability, ensuring safe operation without oscillation.

27. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: LVDTs are ideal for measuring large displacements due to their high resolution and linear response over a wide range.

28. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: A Hall effect sensor detects the interaction between a magnetic field and the current flowing through a conductor.

29. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Feedforward control anticipates disturbances by using predictive inputs and adjusts the system to minimize their impact before they affect the output.

30. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The diaphragm material plays a critical role in the transducer’s temperature range, sensitivity, durability, and ability to resist corrosion.

31. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The Venturi meter operates based on Bernoulli's principle, which relates the pressure and velocity of a fluid in a streamline flow.

32. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Piezoelectric sensors are ideal for measuring dynamic pressures because they respond quickly to rapid changes in pressure.

33. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The derivative term in a PID controller predicts future system errors by analyzing the rate of change in error.

34. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The gauge factor is the ratio of the change in electrical resistance to the mechanical strain applied to the strain gauge.

35. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: RTDs are more suitable for wide temperature ranges due to their linear resistance-temperature relationship.

36. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Feedback gain is a critical factor affecting the stability of a system; incorrect gain settings can lead to oscillations or instability.

37. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Electromagnetic flow meters are ideal for slurries because they do not rely on moving parts and measure using the fluid’s conductivity.

38. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Signal amplification ensures that the sensor output is strong enough to be effectively processed and interpreted by measurement systems.

39. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The Smith predictor compensates for time delays in control systems, thereby improving performance and stability.

40. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Calibration ensures measurement accuracy by comparing sensor outputs to known standards and adjusting for discrepancies.

41. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Capacitive proximity sensors can detect the presence of objects without physical contact, making them suitable for non-invasive applications.

42. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The controller applies corrective actions to the system based on feedback to maintain desired performance.

43. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: An LVDT measures linear displacement by converting it into an electrical signal.

44. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Accelerometers are ideal for vibration monitoring as they measure acceleration forces and can capture dynamic motion.

45. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Proportional control systems cannot eliminate steady-state errors because they do not account for accumulated error over time.

46. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: McLeod gauges are specifically designed for measuring very low pressures, often used in vacuum systems.

47. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hysteresis causes repeatability errors as the output depends on the direction of input changes.

48. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Cascade control systems can improve response to disturbances by using multiple controllers to manage different aspects of the process.

49. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermocouples often produce a non-linear output that requires linearization for accurate temperature measurement.

50. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Air bubbles or particulates in the fluid can scatter ultrasonic waves, reducing the accuracy of measurements.

51. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: An orifice plate relies on Bernoulli's principle, which relates pressure and velocity in a flowing fluid to determine the flow rate from the pressure drop.

52. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: An overly aggressive integral term can introduce instability and cause the system to oscillate excessively.

53. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Calibration should be performed in conditions as close as possible to the expected operating environment to ensure accurate readings.

54. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Strain gauges are the most suitable sensors for measuring deformation or strain in structures under load.

55. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Accurate calibration of the differential pressure transducer is critical to ensure precise measurements of pressure drop.

56. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The Ziegler-Nichols method is a widely used technique for determining the optimal PID controller parameters.

57. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Ultrasonic flow meter accuracy can be influenced by fluid composition, temperature, and particulates, which can alter signal transmission.

58. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Thermistors are highly sensitive to temperature changes and provide rapid response times.

59. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The secondary controller in a cascade control system helps to manage disturbances affecting the primary variable by using a related secondary variable.

60. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Hysteresis introduces systematic error because the output depends on the direction of input change, leading to non-repeatability.

61. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The Pitot tube measures dynamic pressure, and air density is a critical factor in converting dynamic pressure to velocity.

62. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: LVDTs are highly sensitive and accurate devices commonly used for measuring small displacements in precision applications.

63. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Feedforward control predicts disturbances using a model and compensates before they influence the system, enhancing control performance.

64. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Coriolis flow meters can measure the mass flow rate of non-conductive fluids, unlike magnetic flow meters, which rely on fluid conductivity.

65. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Thermistors have a high sensitivity to temperature changes, making them suitable for applications requiring rapid response to temperature variation.

66. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The Smith Predictor is specifically designed to compensate for systems with significant dead time by predicting future states of the process.

67. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: A Wheatstone bridge configuration helps to minimize the impact of temperature variations, enhancing measurement accuracy.

68. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: A tachometer is specifically designed to measure rotational speed in mechanical systems, such as turbines.

69. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Cascade control uses a secondary controller to manage disturbances more effectively, improving the speed and accuracy of the primary process control.

70. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Hysteresis causes non-repeatability errors, as the output depends on the direction of the input change.

71. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Vortex flow meters are ideal for steam flow measurement due to their reliability and ability to handle high-pressure and high-temperature conditions.

72. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The integral term accumulates error over time and eliminates steady-state error by adjusting the control output.

73. Correct Answer: D
   Explanation: The speed of sound in the fluid directly affects the time-of-flight measurement used by ultrasonic sensors, influencing accuracy.

74. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The Ziegler-Nichols method is a heuristic tuning technique that provides initial values for PID parameters to improve system performance.

75. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Magnetoelastic torque sensors are well-suited for measuring torque in rotating shafts, especially in challenging environments such as high temperatures. These sensors rely on the change in magnetic properties of the material under stress, which eliminates the need for physical contact and ensures durability. Strain gauge-based sensors (Option A) require adhesives and can degrade in high temperatures, while capacitive and Hall effect sensors (Options C and D) are not designed for torque measurement in this context.

Practice Test - FE Mechanical - Mechanical Design and Analysis

1. A cylindrical rod with a radius of 10 mm is subjected to a tensile force of 50 kN along its axis. What is the tensile stress experienced by the rod?
   A) 15.92 MPa
   B) 159.2 MPa
   C) 50 MPa
   D) 25 MPa

2. A simply supported beam with a span of 6 m is subjected to a uniformly distributed load of 10 kN/m. What is the maximum bending moment in the beam?
   A) 90 kNm
   B) 120 kNm
   C) 180 kNm
   D) 150 kNm

3. A steel rod is heated from 20°C to 100°C. If the coefficient of thermal expansion is 12 × 10⁻⁶/°C and the modulus of elasticity is 200 GPa, what is the thermal stress generated if the rod is constrained?
   A) 192 MPa
   B) 240 MPa
   C) 1920 MPa
   D) 12 MPa

4. A component is subjected to cyclic loading where σ_max = 400 MPa and σ_min = 100 MPa. What is the stress range in the cycle?
   A) 300 MPa
   B) 500 MPa
   C) 100 MPa
   D) 400 MPa

5. A gear pair has a pinion with 20 teeth and a gear with 40 teeth. If the pinion rotates at 600 RPM, what is the rotational speed of the gear?
   A) 300 RPM
   B) 400 RPM
   C) 600 RPM
   D) 1200 RPM

6. Which material property is most critical for designing components to resist impact loads?
   A) Hardness
   B) Toughness
   C) Elastic Modulus
   D) Tensile Strength

7. A solid circular shaft is designed to transmit 50 kW of power at 300 RPM. What is the required torque for the shaft?
   A) 1592 Nm
   B) 159.2 Nm
   C) 500 Nm
   D) 796 Nm

8. A bolted joint is tightened to achieve a preload of 10 kN. If the bolt has a stiffness of 2 × 10⁶ N/mm and the joint stiffness is 1 × 10⁶ N/mm, what fraction of the load is carried by the bolt?
   A) 0.33
   B) 0.50
   C) 0.66
   D) 0.75

9. A helical spring has a stiffness of 500 N/m and is compressed by 0.2 m. What is the potential energy stored in the spring?
   A) 10 J
   B) 20 J
   C) 50 J
   D) 100 J

10. A ductile material subjected to biaxial stress has principal stresses σ₁ = 300 MPa and σ₂ = 100 MPa. Using the von Mises criterion, what is the equivalent stress?
   A) 200 MPa
   B) 250 MPa
   C) 316 MPa
   D) 400 MPa

11. A rectangular plate with dimensions 200 mm × 400 mm is subjected to a tensile force of 50 kN along its length. If the thickness of the plate is 10 mm, what is the normal stress experienced by the plate?
   A) 62.5 MPa
   B) 12.5 MPa
   C) 25 MPa
   D) 50 MPa

12. Which material property is most relevant when designing components that experience high cyclic stresses?
   A) Hardness
   B) Fatigue strength
   C) Creep resistance
   D) Ductility

13. A slider-crank mechanism has a crank rotating at 300 RPM. If the crank radius is 50 mm, what is the velocity of the slider at the instant the crank is horizontal?
   A) 1.57 m/s
   B) 3.14 m/s
   C) 7.85 m/s
   D) 15.71 m/s

14. A gear train consists of three gears. Gear A has 20 teeth, Gear B has 40 teeth, and Gear C has 80 teeth. If Gear A rotates at 600 RPM, what is the rotational speed of Gear C?
   A) 300 RPM
   B) 150 RPM
   C) 75 RPM
   D) 50 RPM

15. A flat belt transmission system operates between two pulleys with diameters 500 mm and 1000 mm. If the smaller pulley rotates at 1200 RPM, what is the rotational speed of the larger pulley?
   A) 600 RPM
   B) 800 RPM
   C) 1200 RPM
   D) 2400 RPM

16. A steel beam is constrained at both ends and subjected to a temperature increase of 30°C. If the coefficient of thermal expansion is 12 × 10⁻⁶/°C, and the beam's length is 5 m, what is the induced thermal stress assuming no yielding?
   A) 18 MPa
   B) 36 MPa
   C) 72 MPa
   D) 144 MPa

17. A shaft is subjected to torsion with a torque of 200 Nm. If the shaft diameter is 50 mm, what is the maximum shear stress in the shaft?
   A) 25.5 MPa
   B) 40.7 MPa
   C) 52.8 MPa
   D) 67.8 MPa

18. A cantilever beam with length L carries a point load P at the free end. What is the maximum bending moment in the beam?
   A) P × L
   B) P × L / 2
   C) P × L² / 2
   D) P / L

   D) 0.447

   A) 1.33
   B) 1.5
   C) 2.0
   D) 2.67

125. A belt drive system transmits 15 kW of power between two pulleys rotating at 1200 RPM and 600 RPM. If the smaller pulley has a diameter of 0.4 m, what is the tension ratio in the belt assuming a coefficient of friction of 0.3?
   A) 2.56
   B) 3.78
   C) 1.98
   D) 4.12

--- CORRECT ANSWERS AND EXPLANATIONS ---

1. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Tensile stress is calculated using the formula σ = F/A. The area of the cross-section is πr², where r = 10 mm = 0.01 m. Substituting values, σ = (50,000 N) / (π × (0.01 m)²) = 15.92 MPa.

2. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: For a simply supported beam under a uniformly distributed load, the maximum bending moment occurs at the center and is given by M = (wL²) / 8. Substituting w = 10 kN/m and L = 6 m, M = (10 × 6²) / 8 = 90 kNm.

3. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Thermal stress is calculated using the formula σ = EαΔT. Substituting values, σ = (200 × 10⁹ Pa)(12 × 10⁻⁶/°C)(100 − 20 °C) = 192 MPa.

4. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The stress range is defined as σ_range = σ_max − σ_min. Substituting values, σ_range = 400 MPa − 100 MPa = 300 MPa.

5. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The gear ratio is given by the ratio of teeth, Gear Ratio = N_gear/N_pinion = 40/20 = 2. The rotational speed of the gear is ω_gear = ω_pinion / Gear Ratio = 600 RPM / 2 = 300 RPM.

6. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Toughness is the ability of a material to absorb energy and deform plastically without fracturing, making it critical for resisting impact loads.

7. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: Torque is calculated using T = P/ω. Rotational speed ω = (2π × RPM) / 60. Substituting values, T = (50,000 W) / [(2π × 300) / 60] = 1592 Nm.

8. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The load fraction carried by the bolt is given by k_b / (k_b + k_j), where k_b is the bolt stiffness and k_j is the joint stiffness. Substituting values, Load Fraction = (2 × 10⁶) / [(2 × 10⁶) + (1 × 10⁶)] = 0.66.

9. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The potential energy stored in a spring is given by PE = 0.5kx². Substituting k = 500 N/m and x = 0.2 m, PE = 0.5 × 500 × (0.2)² = 50 J.

10. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: The von Mises equivalent stress is given by σ_eq = sqrt(σ₁² − σ₁σ₂ + σ₂²). Substituting values, σ_eq = sqrt((300)² − (300)(100) + (100)²) = 316 MPa.

11. Correct Answer: C
   Explanation: Normal stress is calculated as force divided by the cross-sectional area. Stress = Force / Area = 50,000 / (200 × 10) = 25 MPa.

12. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Fatigue strength is critical in materials subjected to cyclic stresses, as it determines the material's ability to withstand repeated loading without failing.

13. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The velocity of the slider is given by v = ω × r, where ω = 2π × RPM / 60 and r = crank radius. ω = 2π × 300 / 60 = 31.42 rad/s, and v = 31.42 × 0.05 = 1.57 m/s.

14. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: The rotational speed ratio is determined by the teeth ratio. Gear A:B ratio is 20:40 = 1:2, and Gear B:C ratio is 40:80 = 1:2. Thus, Gear C rotates at 600 / 4 = 150 RPM.

15. Correct Answer: A
   Explanation: The speed ratio for the pulleys is inversely proportional to their diameters. Larger pulley speed = (Smaller pulley speed × Smaller pulley diameter) / Larger pulley diameter = (1200 × 500) / 1000 = 600 RPM.

16. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Thermal stress = α × ΔT × E, where α = 12 × 10⁻⁶/°C, ΔT = 30°C, and E (Young's modulus for steel) = 200 GPa. Thermal stress = 12 × 10⁻⁶ × 30 × 200 × 10⁹ = 36 MPa.

17. Correct Answer: B
   Explanation: Maximum shear stress = T × r / J, where J = πd⁴ / 32 for a circular shaft. Substituting values, shear stress = (200 × 0.025) / (π × (0.05)⁴ / 32) = 40.7 MPa.
